Local News

Promotion Association for the New Life Movement to Hold Inaugural Meeting Today 85

With Over a Thousand Attendees Including Mayor Wu and Representatives from All Walks of Life

The Charter and the New Life Covenant Were Passed on the Spot

Seventy-Nine Directors and Forty-One Supervisors Were Elected

A Citizens' Assembly Lantern Parade Is Scheduled for the 15th

The Shanghai New Life Movement Promotion Association will hold its inaugural meeting at 10:00 AM yesterday in the auditorium of the YMCA at Eight Immortals Bridge. Over a thousand people, including Mayor Wu Tiecheng and representatives from all walks of life, attended. The charter and the New Life Covenant were passed on the spot, and Wu Tiecheng and 78 others were elected as directors and Yan Fuqing and 40 others as supervisors. The details are described below:

A Glimpse of the Venue 86

In front of the auditorium, a white banner was hung with the words "Inaugural Meeting of the New Life Movement". The flags of the Party and the nation were forked on either side. Quotations from Chairman Chiang Kai-shek were posted everywhere on the walls, and the decorations were extremely clean and spectacular. Those who attended yesterday were leaders from all walks of life in the city. They all took off their hats and sat solemnly and quietly upon entering the venue, and they were full of energy. Before 10:00 AM, representatives from all walks of life had already gathered, and they adhered to the schedule. This has been rare in various meetings in the past. It is truly a good sign for the start of the New Life Movement in this city.

Representatives from All Walks of Life 87

Yesterday, the representatives from all walks of life who attended included Shanghai Mayor and Garrison Commander Wu Tiecheng, Chief of Staff of the Garrison Command Xu Jinyuan, Secretary-General of the Municipal Government Yu Hongjun, Committee Members of the Municipal Party Department Tao Baichuan, Wu Kaixian, Lu Jingshi, Jiang Huaisu, Director of the Municipal Security Office Yang Hu, Director of the Social Affairs Bureau Wu Xingya, Director of the Public Security Bureau Wen Hongen, Director of the Education Bureau Pan Gongzhan, Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yansong, Ye Jiaxing, Councilor of the Municipal Council Du Yuesheng, China Aviation Association Zhou Nianxing, General Labor Union Zhu Xuefan, Long Peiyun, Jian Xuexiang, President of Jiaotong University Li Zhaohuan, University Federation Li Zhixiang, Xue Guangqian, China Education Federation Chen Jicheng, Secondary School Federation Chen Qimei, Farmers' Association Lu Shikui, as well as representatives from various levels of the Party Department, labor unions, schools, groups, etc., approximately over a thousand people.

(Photograph by Qichang Photography Studio)

Meeting Staff 88

Presidium: Wu Tiecheng, Wu Xingya, Tao Baichuan, Lu Jingshi, Xu Jinyuan, Yuan Bingnan, Chen Jicheng, Yang Hu; Recorder: Du Mengsen; Master of Ceremonies: Zhang Hanyun; Reception: Hu Tianseng, Yang Dean, Shen Liangzhong, Gu Junfeng, Yu Yaoqiu, Huang E, Lin Kecong, Li Erbai, Ren Bin, Xia Weiqing.

Chairman's Report 89

After following the proper protocol, Chairman Wu Tiecheng gave a report, stating that since Chairman Chiang Kai-shek advocated the New Life Movement in Nanchang, all parts of the country have responded successively. Shanghai occupies an important position in the country. Therefore, the Party, government, and military organs have devoted themselves to the preparation of the Shanghai New Life Movement Promotion Association in two weeks. Today, the inaugural meeting is held, and in the future, the work of the New Life Movement will be promoted by the officials selected by the meeting. The name of the Promotion Association, as the words explain, is to promote the realization of the New Life Movement, and its purpose should be to seek its universal implementation. Therefore, the initiators must set an example by implementing it themselves first and serve as a model for the people in order to refresh the public's perception and achieve practical success. Shanghai is the largest port in China. The content of all its social economy and politics is very complex. The population is more than 3 million, which is attached to the vision of the country. Therefore, the need for the New Life Movement goes without saying. However, under these circumstances, how should it be implemented and how should it be universally implemented? It all depends on the work outline planned in the future and the officials elected by the meeting to work hard to achieve it.

Representative Speeches 90

Following that, Pan Gongzhan, representative of the Municipal Party Department, gave a speech, saying that today, the Shanghai New Life Movement Promotion Association is holding its inaugural meeting, and he, on behalf of the Municipal Party Department, is offering his opinions. Since Chairman Chiang Kai-shek initiated the New Life Movement in Nanchang, it has been less than three days, and all parts of the country have been shrouded in this atmosphere, either already implementing it or preparing for it. This movement has been able to be promoted universally for a reason. The occurrence of a movement is not accidental, and its popularity cannot be forced. For example, during the Northern Expedition of the National Revolutionary Army in 1926, who would have expected that the province of Guangdong and a small number of troops could unify the country? At that time, the people were oppressed by the Northern Warlords and sought liberation, so the National Revolution was able to meet the needs of society and create a universal revolutionary atmosphere to promote its success. On the other hand, although the Communist Party also shouted at the top of its lungs to promote communism, it was not adapted to the needs of society, so it has been declining and gradually dying out. The success or failure of a movement depends on whether the initiator has accurately grasped the needs of the guarding association and whether it is suitable for society. Now that Chairman Chiang Kai-shek is advocating the New Life Movement at this time, its importance is no less than that of the National Revolutionary Movement at that time. Now that politics has achieved considerable success, it is necessary to go deeper into society to consolidate the foundation, and the New Life Movement is the movement to reform society. Pan elaborated further on the fact that Chiang Kai-shek's purpose in advocating the New Life Movement is to militarize the lives of the people, and that the four virtues of propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame all contain social trust, not just personal moral cultivation. He also explained that neatness, cleanliness, simplicity, and frugality are easy ways to cultivate propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame.

Discussion of Proposals 91

(1) Pass the charter of the Shanghai New Life Movement Promotion Association; (2) Pass the New Life Covenant; (3) Resolve to organize the Shanghai New Life Experimental Zone, and the Board of Directors will hire experts to draft the measures; (4) Suggest that the conference hold the New Life Movement Week from the 9th of this month to engage in propaganda and stipulate that the first day is for all schools, the second day is for all factories and labor unions, the third day is for all stores and chambers of commerce, the fourth day is for all agricultural areas and farmers' associations, the fifth day is for all Party, government, and military organs, the sixth day is for families, and the seventh day is for the general public. On this day, a general meeting of citizen representatives will be held, and a lantern parade will be held in the evening.

Passing of the Charter 92

Charter of the Shanghai New Life Movement Promotion Association, Chapter I, General Provisions, Article 1, This association is named the Shanghai New Life Movement Promotion Association. Article 2, The purpose of this association is to promote propriety, righteousness, integrity, shame, responsibility, discipline, and cleanliness in order to rejuvenate the Chinese nation. Article 3, This association and its branch associations shall be located in this city. Chapter II, Membership, Article 4, Any citizen of this city who is willing to abide by the New Life Covenant prescribed by this association and abide by the charter of this association, with the introduction of one member and the approval of the Board of Directors, may become a member of this association. Article 5, Members of this association shall pay annual membership fees of two cents to two yuan, which shall be determined and paid by the members. Article 6, Members of this association shall have the right to elect and be elected, and other rights that they should enjoy. Article 7, If a member of this association violates the New Life Covenant of this association or damages the reputation of this association, they may be punished separately in accordance with the following clauses: (1) Warning; (2) Expulsion from membership; (3) Those who violate the law shall be dealt with according to law. Chapter III, Organization, Article 8, The highest authority of this association shall be the General Assembly of Members or the General Assembly of Member Representatives. During the adjournment period, the Board of Directors shall be the executive body and the Board of Supervisors shall be the supervisory body. Article 9, This association shall elect 79 directors and 41 alternate directors through the General Assembly of Members or the General Assembly of Member Representatives to form the Board of Directors to handle all matters of this association and elect 41 supervisors and 17 alternate supervisors to form the Board of Supervisors to manage the supervisory affairs of this association. The term of office for directors and supervisors shall be one year, and they may be re-elected. Article 10, The Board of Directors of this association shall elect one chairman and 21 standing directors from among the directors, and the Board of Supervisors shall elect 11 standing supervisors from among the supervisors to preside over the daily affairs of each association. Article 11, The Board of Directors of this association shall have four groups: general affairs, organization, propaganda, and guidance. Each group shall have one director and several staff members. The Board of Supervisors shall have one secretary and several staff members. Article 12, This association may establish a design committee, which shall be organized by members hired by the Board of Directors. Article 13, This association may organize branch associations in schools, institutions, factories, stores, urban areas, etc., and the measures shall be formulated separately. Branch associations may establish sub-associations, and the measures shall be formulated separately. Article 14, The General Assembly of Members or the General Assembly of Member Representatives of this association shall be held once a year, and shall be convened by the Board of Directors. In case of necessity, it may be convened temporarily by the Board of Directors. Article 15, If the General Assembly of Members or the General Assembly of Member Representatives of this association is adjourned due to insufficient quorum, the members present may hold a provisional resolution and send it to the Board of Directors to send a letter to each member to vote in writing on the provisional resolution, and the one with more votes in agreement shall be passed. Article 16, The Board of Directors and the Board of Supervisors of this association shall hold a meeting once a month, which shall be convened separately by the standing directors and the standing supervisors. Chapter IV, Funding, Article 17, The funds of this association shall be supplemented by the following items: (1) Membership fees; (2) Special donations; (3) Subsidies. Chapter V, Supplementary Provisions, Article 18, If there are any matters not covered in this charter, they may be amended by the General Assembly of Members or the General Assembly of Member Representatives. Article 19, This charter shall be passed by the General Assembly of Members or the General Assembly of Member Representatives and reported to the Shanghai Special Municipality Party Department and the Municipal Government for record.

Passing of Public Covenants 93

(1) Regarding Food: 1. Eat properly. 2. Sit up straight. 3. Do not throw food scraps. 4. Do not make noise when eating or chewing. 5. Do not smoke. 6. Do not drink excessively. 7. Do not eat snacks. 8. Drink several cups of boiled water upon waking. 9. Do not eat unclean food. 10. Do not drink unboiled water. 11. Always rinse your mouth after eating; brush your teeth every morning. 12. Do not engage in strenuous exercise before or after eating. 13. Strive for cleanliness in the kitchen and with utensils. (2) Regarding Clothing: 1. Dress plainly, neatly, and cleanly. 2. Button buttons properly. 3. Wear shoes and socks properly. 4. Wear hats straight. 5. Remove hats when saluting. 6. Remove hats in assembly halls. 7. Do not wear hats indoors. 8. Mend torn clothing. 9. Use domestic products for clothing. 10. Do not hang clothes on the street to dry. 11. Always carry a handkerchief. (3) Regarding Housing: 1. Keep the house clean and tidy. 2. Do not deface walls. 3. Keep furniture simple. 4. Keep doors and windows open frequently. 5. Wake up and go to bed early. 6. Rinse your mouth, wash your hair, and wash your hands frequently. 7. Breathe fresh air. 8. Engage in some appropriate form of exercise every day. 9. Keep nails trimmed. 10. Bathe frequently. 11. Sun and wash bedding regularly. 12. Pay attention to children's hygiene. 13. Sweep the house often. 14. Dredge ditches frequently. 15. Keep tables and chairs clean. 16. Keep toilets clean. 17. Eradicate mosquitoes. 18. Eradicate flies. 19. Kill rats. 20. Do not spit anywhere. 21. Do not urinate or defecate anywhere. 22. Dispose of trash in trash cans. 23. Every household should sweep the street in front of their door every day. (4) Regarding Travel: 1. Walk on the left side. 2. Do not rush ahead when walking. 3. Do not walk too slowly. 4. Do not eat while walking. 5. Say "I'm sorry" if you accidentally bump into someone while walking. 6. When buying tickets at the station, proceed in an orderly line. 7. When boarding and disembarking at piers, or getting on and off vehicles, proceed in an orderly line. 8. In public places, proceed in an orderly line. 9. Say "Good morning" when you meet someone in the morning. 10. Say "Goodbye" when parting. 11. Return found items to their original owner. 12. Cherish public property. 13. Help women, children, the elderly, and the weak when getting on and off vehicles. 14. Do not talk or laugh loudly when on boats or vehicles. 15. Do not urinate anywhere. (5) Regarding Work: 1. Be focused, persistent, and sincere in your work. 2. Work hard and endure hardship without complaint. 3. Do today's work today. 4. Adhere to office hours. 5. Obey orders, accept guidance, and abide by rules. 6. Establish a plan before starting work. 7. Do not flinch or shirk responsibility when encountering difficulties at work. 8. Do not cause trouble when there is none, and do not fear trouble when it arises. 9. Do not be discouraged or surrender when subjected to unfair attacks. 10. Do not take undeserved money, receive undeserved praise, or be greedy for undeserved benefits. 11. Maintain an optimistic attitude at work. 12. Do not look down on labor or laborers. 13. Transactions must be fair. (6) Regarding Education: 1. Know at least one thousand Chinese characters. 2. Read the newspaper every day. 3. Understand major events at home and abroad. 4. Pay attention to and study new things. 5. Frequently participate in beneficial gatherings. 6. Adhere to "preliminary civil rights" at gatherings. 7. Do not set a bad example for children. (7) Regarding Entertainment: 1. Do not get angry easily when feeling agitated. 2. Find joy in everyday life. 3. Control your temper and prevent it from erupting. 4. Do not gamble or dance with prostitutes. 5. Do not gamble. 6. Do not read obscene books or look at obscene pictures. 7. Choose a proper form of entertainment. 8. Do not become addicted to or linger in any form of entertainment. (8) Regarding Socializing: 1. Be punctual for appointments. 2. Wait for others to finish speaking before speaking. 3. Do not chat with visitors for more than fifteen minutes. 4. Do not laugh and joke at funerals. 5. Mediate when others are fighting. 6. Do not curse or hit others. 7. Reason with people in all matters; do not quarrel. 8. Reason with people who insult you unreasonably; do not endure it casually. 9. Speak politely. 10. Apologize when you have offended someone. 11. Respect elders when you see them. 12. Be courteous to women. 13. Be trustworthy to friends. 14. Listen quietly to others when they speak to me. 15. Be quiet at meetings and performances. 16. Reduce unnecessary social engagements. 17. Be thrifty at weddings and funerals. 18. Do not offer cigarettes to guests. 19. Do not borrow money from people unless absolutely necessary.

New Timetable for Two Railway Lines Implemented Yesterday 100

Three-Day Tourist Train Added on Shanghai-Hangzhou Section

Ticket Revenue at North Railway Station of Two Lines Increased by Ten Thousand Yuan Yesterday

The new timetable for the main lines of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways was implemented yesterday, and a tourist train was added to the Shanghai-Hangzhou section. The ticket revenue has greatly increased. The details are as follows:

The new timetable for the two railway lines was implemented yesterday. Except for the Shanghai-Songjiang section and the Cao'e River-Ningbo section, which remain the same, the timetable for the main lines of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou was revised and implemented yesterday. The Shanghai North Railway Station departure time for the No. 302 Shanghai-Beijing train was changed to 4:05 PM. The Beijing North Railway Station departure time for the No. 301 Beijing-Shanghai train was changed to 3:05 PM. The departure times for other trains in both directions were also changed. Although yesterday was a Sunday, the inquiry offices at the North Railway Station of both lines and the business offices in the north and south of the city were open as usual, and additional staff were assigned. The workload was very heavy. For the North Railway Station inquiry office alone, there were more than 10,000 requests for timetables from all sectors yesterday.

Revenue Increase: Yesterday was the first day of the new timetable's implementation. The Director of the Transportation Department, Xiao Weiguo, and the two Deputy Directors, Yuan and Wang, were all on duty as usual and opened tourist trains. The Shanghai North Railway Station departure time was 1:00 PM, and the arrival time in Hangzhou was 5:40 PM. The Hangzhou departure time was 6:55 PM, and the arrival time at the Shanghai North Railway Station was 11:25 PM. The service ran from the 1st to the 3rd. Yesterday was the Western New Year, and the weather was very good. Travelers were very crowded. The ticket revenue for both railway lines increased by more than 10,000 yuan compared to usual.

Chairman Chiang Kai-shek Replied to Ningbo Native Association 101

The Conscription of the Reserve Force Has Been Ordered to be Handled Cautiously

Since the Zhejiang Provincial Government ordered all counties to conscript a reserve force for the militia, there have been misunderstandings among the people, and they have been avoiding conscription. The Ningbo people in Shanghai have repeatedly received complaints from their hometowns, stating that the conscription would hinder agricultural work since the spring planting season is in full swing. They sent telegrams to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek in Nanchang and the Zhejiang Provincial Government, appealing for the people's sake. The details have been reported in this newspaper. It is now known that the association received a reply telegram from Chairman Chiang Kai-shek yesterday (abbreviated title): "The telegram has been noted and has been forwarded to the Zhejiang Provincial Government for cautious handling. Chiang Kai-shek, Jian; Xing Zhi, One Seal."

General Assembly of Customs Declaration Workers Decides to Strike 103

Shanghai Group Workers to Implement Today

Xin Sheng News Agency reports that, regarding the Tianjin Group Customs Declaration Firm's cancellation of cartage fees, the customs declaration workers held an emergency general assembly at the union hall in the city at 4:00 PM yesterday. More than 200 members and supervisors attended, and Ren Xixiang was publicly elected as chairman. The atmosphere was quite tense. All members demanded that the union issue an emergency order for a general strike. After persuasion by the supervisors, it was resolved that: (1) The Shanghai Group members will implement a strike starting tomorrow (i.e., today). (2) The union will request the Party and government organs to convene a mediation as soon as possible. (3) A 64-member investigation team will be organized to patrol the docks and shipheads. If a member has a dispute, the investigation team will be responsible for advising and preventing riots.

The Ministry of Communications' Telephone Bureau Takes Over the Minhang Town Telephone Service 104

In Response to Requests from Town Users and the County Magistrate

After Sending Personnel to Inspect, a Request has been Submitted to the Ministry for Instructions

The telephone users in Minhang Town, Shanghai County, requested that County Magistrate Pan Zhongjia plan a reform because the telephones were old and the sound was weak. There are a total of more than 30 telephones in the Minhang District, which are concurrently operated by the Shanghai-Minhang Long-Distance Bus Company. County Magistrate Pan Zhongjia stated that telephones are not only essential for transportation but also have a significant impact on commerce. Therefore, he contacted Xu Xueyu, the Director of the Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, and Yu Bingjian, the Chief Engineer, to have the Telephone Bureau manage the improvement. The Telephone Bureau sent Yu Bingjian to inspect and has submitted a request to the ministry for instructions. It is reported that if the Telephone Bureau takes over and the number of users increases in the future, a branch bureau will be established. Otherwise, the lines and telephones will be reformed to facilitate use.

Supervisor Liu Did Not Come to Shanghai to Investigate the Case 105

A Letter from the Secretariat of the Control Yuan States that: "Having read the Shen Bao report on March 27th, regarding the Supervisor coming to Shanghai to investigate the case of the President of the District Court being accused, it stated, 'This Yuan sent Supervisor Liu San to Shanghai to secretly investigate.' Upon investigation, I was not sent to Shanghai to investigate the case. The alleged accusation is completely inaccurate, and the praise for President Shen's efforts is completely fabricated. The Secretariat should immediately send a letter to the Shen Bao to make an important statement in the original location to avoid spreading falsehoods and clarify the truth." The Secretariat of the Control Yuan, March 31st.

Extraordinary General Meeting of the Bar Association Adjourned Due to Lack of Quorum 106

The Shanghai Bar Association convened an extraordinary general meeting of members yesterday (Sunday) at the Lake Society on the second floor of the intersection of Beijing Road and Guizhou Road in the Public Concession to discuss the mandated revision of the association's articles of association and the restoration of the president's council system prior to 1927. From 2:00 PM to 4:00 PM, members arrived in succession, totaling 179 people. Tao Baichuan from the Municipal Party Department, Ouyang Shu from the Shanghai District Court, Guo Wei from the First Special District, Wang Ren from the Second Special District, and the Third Prosecutor attended the meeting to supervise and guide. The proceedings of the meeting were as follows: (1) The meeting was called to order by ringing a bell. (2) The presidium, consisting of Chen Tingrui and Wang Weizhen, took office. (3) All stood at attention and bowed three times to the Party and National flags. (4) Chairman Chen Tingrui respectfully read the will of the Premier. (5) Three minutes of silence. (6) Report of matters: (A) The Chairman reported that the association had a total of 1,098 members. According to the legal quorum, one-quarter, or 275 people, must be present. Those present today did not meet the legal quorum, so the meeting had to be adjourned, and a discussion meeting would be held instead. Personnel sent by various agencies would leave first. (B) The Chairman reported that the association's opposition to the court's collection of attorney notification fees had been jointly submitted to the Judicial Administration Department by the four associations of Jiangning, Zhenjiang, other counties, and this association, requesting a halt to the collection, but it had not been approved. It was now resolved to continue the struggle, and Yu Zhongluo et al. were being designated to draft a continued petition. (C) A report on the circumstances of the District Court's detention center refusing lawyers to meet with detainees. (7) Matters to be discussed: (A) The association's executive and supervisory committee proposed amendments to the articles of association. (B) Member Tang Yingsong proposed adding an economic management committee to the articles of association. (C) Member Xu Zuoliang proposed that the constitution should stipulate the independence of judicial funding and guarantee the independence fund. (D) Member Xu Zuoliang proposed that the court should sell official papers at cost and pay interest on the money paid by the parties. (E) Member Yan Lunkuai proposed that the current president of the association should determine the standards for promotion. (F) Member Wu Guochang proposed that Articles 9, 11, 20, 31-33, etc. of the articles of association should be amended, and additions and deletions should be made to the articles. (G) Shi Qinghua, Zhang Feixiong, Wang Xianggu, and others expressed their opinions. Since the meeting could not be convened, and the discussion meeting had no voting rights, they requested a suitable method of discussion to convene a general meeting as soon as possible. As a result, it was decided that there was no need to hold a discussion meeting, and it was decided to postpone the meeting for three weeks and reconvene an extraordinary general meeting of members. The meeting was then adjourned.

Municipal Land Bureau Limits Gaogiao Concealed Reclamation, Each Household to Report 114

Deadline is the End of April This Year

Those Who Fail to Report by the Deadline Will Be Strictly Punished

The Shanghai Municipal Land Bureau, in order to comply with the order to rectify the coastal sandbanks of Gaoqiao, hereby announces to all households engaged in concealed reclamation that they must come to the bureau to report in detail before the end of April. The original text is as follows: It is hereby ordered by the Municipal Government, in accordance with the notification from the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance, regarding the coastal sandbanks of Gaoqiao, as reported by the Shangbao Sand Field Official Property Bureau, that the concealed reclamation households are reaping the benefits, etc., and requesting investigation and handling. As it concerns public income, detailed investigation and practical handling are required, and a report is to be submitted, etc. It is our duty to comply. Upon investigation, the coastal sandbanks of Gaoqiao originally belonged to public land. Except for those coastal households who previously obtained property certificates from the state and local administrative organs, and have paid grain taxes, which should be recognized as their property, those who have reclaimed and cultivated privately without any documents are considered to be engaged in concealed reclamation. For the sake of rectification, we hereby issue a notice to inform all relevant property owners that if there are any cases of concealed reclamation, they must, before the end of April this year, submit a written statement to this bureau, stating the location, boundaries, and area of the concealed land, and attaching a sketch map. After measurement, those that are found to be not obstructive to the embankment will be allowed to pay the price and increase the grain tax for management. Those who conceal and fail to report beyond the deadline will be strictly punished in the future. Do not delay and mislead yourselves. This notice.

Provisional Meeting of the Lake Society Executive Committee 115

At 10:00 AM on April 1st, the Lake Society convened a second provisional meeting of the Executive Committee to discuss issues such as the restoration of the Huzhou Guild Hall and the construction of the Huzhou Middle School building. In the afternoon of the same day, a banquet was held at the Guild Hall for Huzhou fellow villagers. More than a dozen executive committee members including Wang Yiting, Chen Aishi, Shen Tianxin, Chen Guofu, Pan Gongzhan, and Yan Junyi, and more than a dozen fellow villagers including Wu Daquan, Zhang Danru, and Shen Zhongyi attended. The meeting issues are recorded below: (1) Restoration of the Huzhou Guild Hall: The Huzhou Guild Hall is located near the Shanghai North Railway Station in Zhabei. It was founded by prominent Huzhou merchants in Shanghai such as Yang Xinzhi, Zhu Wulou, and Shen Lianfang. The buildings were magnificent and large-scale. Since 1926, the buildings have been damaged due to being stationed by troops. During the Shanghai Battle in 1932, the Guild Hall was located in a strategic position and was often stationed by troops, resulting in it being bombed by the Japanese, destroying part of the buildings and mortuary. The damage is deeply regrettable. It is now planned to repair and restore it. (2) Construction of the Huzhou Middle School building: The Huzhou Shanghai Primary School has been established for more than twenty years and has a long history. However, due to financial limitations, the school does not have its own building. Since Mr. Yan Junyi became the principal, he has strengthened the rectification, and the school affairs have been progressing day by day, and the number of students has been increasing day by day. The rented private houses are sometimes insufficient for use, and the rent is extremely high, which is not economical. Therefore, it is planned to build a school building to expand. It is heard that the above two proposals have been fully approved by the Executive Committee, and Wang Yiting, Chen Lantu, Chen Guofu, Shen Tianxin, Shen Lianfang, Qian Xinzhi, Pan Gongzhan, Wu Daquan, Liu Zhengru, Pang Laichen, Zhang Danru, and others have been publicly elected as restoration committee members to be responsible for planning everything. In addition, the Lake Society on Guizhou Road originally had a three-story building. Recently, the society's affairs have been expanding day by day, and the original building is no longer sufficient. It is now planned to add another floor on the original site to add a dormitory for fellow villagers and a library for the vocational training school. It is heard that when the society was built, it was originally planned to have four floors, but due to insufficient funds, three floors were built first. Therefore, the foundation is very solid. Although another floor is being added now, it does not affect the original foundation at all, and the structural strength is sufficient to carry the load. It is heard that it has been decided to hand it over to the Standing Committee for handling.

Xu Shiying Writes to Request Relief for Disaster Victims in Various Counties of Anhui Province 116

Relief Has Not Been Organized for Refugees Who Fled Previously

These Refugees Have Been Fleeing for About Six Years

The great philanthropist Xu Shiying of this city wrote a letter to the Xinwei Relief Society yesterday to request relief for disaster victims in Lihuang and other places in western Anhui, saying: "Respected Sirs, the various counties in western Anhui have long been under bandit occupation and have been successively recovered by Chairman Liu of the Anhui Provincial Government leading troops to suppress the bandits. The refugees who have been moved out urgently need relief. A temporary immigration work team has been specially established, and Mr. Xu Xinxuan is invited to preside over it, and Zhang Zepu is retained to assist. Recently, Mr. Xu and Mr. Zhang telegraphed that the disaster victims were gathered in Lihuang Mapu, Yeji, and Kaishun Street. What I saw with my own eyes was tragic. It is estimated that there are more than 5,000 people in Lihuang, more than 2,000 people in Mapu, more than 3,000 people in Yeji, and 500 people in Kaishun. The reception facilities set up this time are all newly moved out from the front line. Relief has not been organized for refugees who fled previously. It has been about six years since these refugees fled. Apart from those who died due to hunger and disease and those who fled far away, who are not included, at the time of the army's encirclement and suppression, the time to clear the bandits seems to be after three or four months. The refugees are now exhausted and it is not easy to overcome this difficult situation. I sincerely pray that you will save people thoroughly and consult with the Red Cross Society Shi Zila, Wang Peila, Yu Qiala, Wen Lanla, Jixianhui Wang Yila, Huang Hanla, Li Shoushan, Zhu Shouchcheng, Feng Yangshan, Mr. Guang Jiong of the Buddhist Association Zhi, Qian Jinping, Huang Bodu, and gentlemen, and charitable organizations, to show great compassion and collect funds for relief. At the current price of grain, it seems that about two yuan per person can save these ten thousand lives. If you do not try your best to plead on their behalf, I am afraid that they will starve to death. I sincerely hope that you will consider it. I have long admired your association's commitment to saving people and your enthusiasm for relief. Over the years, the disaster areas in the province have repeatedly received your generous donations, either by sending personnel for disaster relief or by allocating funds for relief. The disaster victims have benefited greatly. I hope that you will consider the urgency of waiting after this disaster and raise a large sum of money to save the remaining people. Then, your kindness will be appreciated immeasurably. Apart from sending separate letters, I am writing to inform you accordingly. I hope you will check and reply."

Proposal to Improve Cigarette Tax System Presents Concrete Measures 130

Tax Should Be Levied in Seven Grades in Accordance With Regulations

This Can Enrich the National Treasury and Benefit Chinese Merchants

Xin Sheng News Agency reports that 24 Chinese cigarette factories in this city, including the Minzhong Cigarette Company, have jointly petitioned the Yuan and Ministry to improve the current cigarette tax system, which is biased and unfair. The Tax Department has sent the original petition to the Chinese Cigarette Factory Association for review and reply. The association has also sent a letter to Huang Ziping of the original proposer Minzhong Cigarette Company, asking him to draft a practical proposal for discussion at the meeting. It is learned that Mr. Huang has replied to the association yesterday, proposing detailed measures, which are recorded below:

Reply to the Association 131

Direct reply: I have received your letter and am aware of everything. Regarding the case of improving the tax rate, the members' meeting previously publicly elected Ziping and eight others as review committee members. They held a meeting and prepared a written opinion on the review of this case, which was sent by your association to the Tax Department for record. The original written opinion stated, "The Regulations on Unified Cigarette Tax were promulgated by the National Government. Article 3 of the regulations stipulates that all goods manufactured in the country should be graded according to the customs valuation standard, i.e., seven grades. The tax silver is calculated according to a percentage, i.e., tax is levied on value. The seven-grade system and the principle of levying tax on value were the same for the previous unified cigarette tax, the current customs duties, and the current cigar tax. It is better than the current arbitrary and mandatory cigarette tax, which has no standard. It is fair to pay 32.5 percent of the unified cigarette tax, because the customs valuation is the standard. What is currently requested from the government is to handle it in accordance with the effective Regulations on Unified Cigarette Tax promulgated by the government, without destroying the promulgated tax law. If it is said that the finances are stretched and additional funds must be raised, relief can be sought in the law and an appropriate increase can be made to 42.5 percent or 52.5 percent. How can the fair seven-grade tax system and the principle of levying tax on value be broken? I believe that if the government is prudent, it can organize a cigarette tax rate review committee, with several committee members from the Legislative Yuan, the Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Industry, and the Tax Department, and several committee members elected by the Chinese Cigarette Factory Association, to gather together for open discussion, so as to determine a perfect tax rate, which can meet the needs of the government in terms of finance, promote the development of the social economy, and adapt to the people's ability to bear it." These are my claims, which have been passed by a majority of the review committee members elected by the general meeting and sent by the association to the Tax Department. The iron case is like a mountain, and I do not need to propose another opinion. The case passed by a majority of the review committee members elected by the general meeting cannot be overthrown illegally by a minority. The Tax Department has not replied to this case for a long time. Your association, entrusted by the general meeting, should request the Tax Department to handle it quickly in accordance with the original written opinion in order to conform to public opinion. I am replying accordingly to your letter for your reference. Sincerely, to the Shanghai Chinese Cigarette Factory Association.

The hidden worries of the economic downturn are lurking here. Therefore, we should abandon the attitude of sticking to old ways, change to scientific methods, and harvest abundantly. Increasing production is inevitable. I sincerely hope that you will all work hard after visiting, etc.

Determining Principles 137

Based on the seven-tier tax plan, the following two principles are combined: (A) The new tax rate tiers should follow Article 3 of the Cigarette Tax Regulations, using customs valuation as the standard, still divided into seven tiers. The selling price per carton is assumed to be the same as that set during the old seven-tier tax era. (B) The tax per carton under the new tax rate should follow the principle of ad valorem tax, assumed to be 52.5 percent. Based on the above two principles and referring to the 1929 tax rate table, a provisional new tax rate table is as follows: (1) Assuming the new tax rate table is for 50,000 cigarettes per carton, those with a registered selling price of 1,052 yuan or more will pay a first-tier tax of 653 yuan, 6 jiao, and 2.5 fen; those with a registered selling price of 714 yuan or more will pay a second-tier tax of 417 yuan, 3 jiao, and 7.5 fen; those with a registered selling price of 546 yuan or more will pay a third-tier tax of 299 yuan, 2 jiao, and 5 fen; those with a registered selling price of 378 yuan or more will pay a fourth-tier tax of 220 yuan, 5 jiao; those with a registered selling price of 253 yuan or more will pay a fifth-tier tax of 149 yuan, 6 jiao, and 2.5 fen; those with a registered selling price of 125 yuan or more will pay a sixth-tier tax of 86 yuan, 6 jiao, and 2.5 fen; those with a registered selling price of less than 125 yuan will pay a seventh-tier tax of 47 yuan, 2 jiao, and 5 fen. According to the above provisional new tax rate table, the products of Chinese merchants will generally fall under the fourth, fifth, sixth, and seventh tiers, with the sixth and seventh tiers being the most common. Therefore, the tax burden borne by Chinese merchants will mostly be over 86 yuan or over 47 yuan per carton, which is less than the current tax rate. British and American products, on the other hand, will cover all seven tiers, with some requiring a tax increase to over 650 yuan per carton, which is more than the current tax rate. According to this increase and decrease, based on the number of cigarette cartons sold in Shanghai in February, the increased burden on British and American companies is about 60,000 yuan. For Chinese merchants, those whose main business is high-end cigarettes will see an increase, while those whose main business is low-end cigarettes will see a decrease. For example, considering East China, the February sales of "20-pack Betel Nut" were 80 cartons, and "10-pack Anle" were 240 cartons, both of which can be changed to the seventh tier. If calculated using the provisional tax rate, the monthly tax paid will be about 10,000 yuan less than the current tax rate. Considering Central and South China, "10-pack Da Zhonghua" can be changed to the seventh tier, with monthly sales of 120 cartons. If calculated using the provisional tax rate, the monthly tax paid will be about 3,600 yuan less than the current tax rate. In this way, the tax on high-end cigarettes is increased, and the tax on low-end cigarettes is decreased. In terms of tax rate, it is consistently 52.5 per 100 in value, without any unfairness. The burden on Chinese merchants is reduced, so that they will not be oppressed by foreign merchants from the outside or encroached upon by smuggled cigarettes from the inside. The future of the cigarette industry will surely improve. Government tax revenue, based on the number of cigarette cartons sold in Shanghai in February, can also increase by more than 79,000 yuan. If extrapolated to the whole country, it will be even more considerable. If the cigarette tax is reduced, the cost will be lower, and smuggled cigarettes will have no opportunity to encroach, so tax revenue can be expected to improve even more. This tax rate benefits the government above, benefits Chinese merchants below, and benefits domestic tobacco farmers on the side. The tax rate is levied ad valorem, which is a common taxation principle, and is also clearly stipulated in the Cigarette Unified Tax Regulations. It is fair and impartial, and foreigners cannot use it as an excuse to oppose it. It is fair and easy to implement, and there is nothing better than this. It is believed that the quality of the tax rate is very important to the business. If all colleagues compare their products with the provisional tax rate and the current tax rate, they will realize the advantages and disadvantages.

Double-Decker Buses Began Running Yesterday 138

The double-deckers that have arrived will run as soon as they are installed.

Prices Increased on Routes 1, 2, 3, 4, 8, and 10 Yesterday

The British-owned China General Omnibus Company, with the approval of the Municipal Council, is operating double-decker buses. The original petition is recorded below:

Hu Ganqing's Concubine Sues for Inheritance, Settlement Unsuccessful 140

Hu Xue, with her daughter, came to court to demand inheritance.

The amount in dispute between the two sides is too far apart.

Hu Ganqing, a shareholder of Fuchang Ginseng Store in the South City and Hu Qingyutang Pharmacy in Beijing Road, Hangzhou, passed away in 1929, leaving behind several wives and concubines. Recently, Hu Xue, a concubine of Ganqing from Suzhou, hired lawyer Lu Dingkui to sue Ganqing's son, Shanqing, in the Civil Court of the First Special District, demanding the division of the estate, estimated at 300,000 yuan, one-third of which, etc. The court has held two trials, and the details have been recorded in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Shen Hong came to the Civil Court No. 6 to continue the hearing. Both parties appeared in person. The judge first asked whether a settlement had been attempted during the adjournment. According to the defendant's representatives, lawyers Lu Shaozong and Lin Yingqing, the plaintiff insisted on 30,000 yuan, while the defendant only offered several thousand yuan, resulting in

No Settlement 141

Therefore, Hu Xue stated that due to the high cost of living, this small amount of several thousand yuan was not enough to cover expenses, and she was not deliberately extravagant. The court then advised both parties to make concessions and sought the defendant's opinion. The defendant, Hu Shanqing, said, "I have no obligation to support the plaintiff and am unwilling to make concessions." The court then instructed him, "Whether the plaintiff is your father's concubine or mistress, your father did support her while he was alive. Therefore, I am now advising you to increase the amount slightly so that a settlement can be reached." The defendant stated that he could offer at most 3,000 yuan, and could not add more. Since the plaintiff, Hu Xue, was unwilling to make concessions, a settlement was difficult to achieve, and the court began to

Proceed with the Trial 142

According to Hu Xue, she met Hu Ganqing around 1916 or 1917, and in 1918, she gave birth to a daughter named Qiaoyun, who is now 17 years old, at Wu Cui's house in Laohui Le Lane. At that time, Ganqing lived in Sanjiajian, and I could not come forward, so Hu instructed me to go to my mother's house in Suzhou temporarily, etc. In addition, Hu Shizhen, the son of Hu Shanqing, stated that he was 14 years old, lived in Jiuqu Lane, Hangzhou, and was currently studying in the first grade of Huilan Elementary School. The plaintiff was my grandfather's mistress and previously lived at No. 10 Xinglongfang, Chongqing Road. I have been there. Although I have seen her daughter, Qiaoyun, I do not know her. When my grandfather was seriously ill, the plaintiff came to my house and told me to

Come and Play 143

I took the opportunity to go, calling the plaintiff "Grandma" because she was older than my mother. After I went to Hangzhou, I sent a letter to the plaintiff, calling her "Concubine Grandmother." The court then gave him several letters to read. Shizhen replied that they were not written by him. He was then ordered to write numbers with a fountain pen for handwriting comparison. in Xujiahui. Ganqing was my father. Since my father passed away, I have been to the old house on Guling Road and wore mourning clothes. Fuchang Ginseng Store 145

at the end of 1926. By the end of 1928, the store could not open the dividend account due to the large amount of money used under Hu Ganqing's account. Rampant Pirates 146

Destroying the fishing industry, earnestly request strict suppression, in order to maintain maritime security and protect the livelihood of merchants and people. The members of our association all engage in offshore fishing. We usually lend money to fishermen to go fishing, and only when the fishing boats return can the loans be repaid. Fishing merchants and fishermen depend on each other. If there is a concern about the decline of fishing villages, then there is a concern about the collapse of the fish market. The situation has been fraught with difficulties for many years, and maritime bandits are rampant.

The Coasts of Jiangsu and Zhejiang 147

Have become havens for fugitives. It is not that there are no naval ships to protect the sea, and it is also the duty of specialized officers to arrest criminals. It is simply because

The soldiers are not well-trained for long, and the officials have no fixed responsibilities. They indulge in the habit of stealing and playing, and use their petty cleverness to allow the fish in the jar to transform into whales on the sea. Robbing ships is treated as a common occurrence. How can these small fishing families have the strength to resist? In recent years, coastal fishing villages have been on the verge of desolation, and the fish market has been affected, making it difficult to maintain. The cunning ones then

Collude with the Japanese 148

To sell Japanese fish, while the members of our association rely on a single, unyielding heart. In the midst of economic panic, they try their best to cope, but it is difficult to survive. We believe that fishing merchants and fishermen are all under the protection of the country, and your Excellency's concern for the suffering of our local area is understandable. The only solution is to combine all maritime anti-piracy agencies and place them directly under the jurisdiction of the Ministry of the Navy. Then, select specialized personnel to

Comprehensively Pacify and Suppress 149

Divide the coastal areas into several security zones based on the terrain, and allocate warships and personnel accordingly. The dens on land should be secretly investigated, and the havens at sea should be patrolled frequently. Then, the pirates' support will be exhausted and their reinforcements will be cut off. In just a few months, they can be eliminated. This will not only save the fishing merchants from the brink of extinction, but also strengthen national prestige in times of difficulty. We urgently submit our plea, hoping for your wise consideration and appropriate action. Respectfully submitted by the Shanghai Salted Fish Industry Association.

Appeal Rejected in Jealousy and Adultery Case 158

Jin Peifang Still Sentenced to Eight Years in Prison

Jin Peifang, a 20-year-old young man from Dongtai, was working as a shop assistant in a Westerner's home at No. 96 Verdun Garden, Albert Road, French Concession. He and Sheng Qinhuang, a 21-year-old Ningbo man who was also working as a butler, were jealous of each other because they both loved Chen Aqin, a maid who worked with them. On the morning of November 10 of the previous year, at around 3:00 AM, Jin took advantage of Sheng's sleep and used a wood-chopping knife to injure Sheng's head and pull out his testicles on both sides. Fortunately, the spermatic cords were not injured, and Sheng's life was saved. The police arrested Jin and sent him to the Second Special District Court, where he was prosecuted for attempted murder. After a trial, Jin was found guilty of intentionally causing serious injury and sentenced to eight years in prison. Jin was dissatisfied with the verdict and decided to hire a lawyer on his behalf, Jin Zhixiang, his father, to file an appeal with the Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. The High Court opened a hearing based on the petition, and the details have been reported in previous issues. The case has now concluded. On the afternoon of the previous day, the High Court, led by Judge Guo, together with Judges Sun and Fan, opened a hearing and ordered the appellant, Jin Peifang, to be brought before the court. The appeal was rejected, and Jin was returned to custody to await the final determination of the third-instance appeal period, after which he will be sent to prison to serve his sentence.

The Divorce Case of Shen Baigui Reopened for Debate 159

The Witness Invited by Shen Baigui

Is She an Aunt or a Biological Mother?

Shen Baigui, a 24-year-old woman from Songjiang, was married to Zhang Guifu from Chuansha through a matchmaker. They have one son and one daughter. Recently, because Zhang had an affair and neglected his wife, Shen hired lawyer Chen Xuelu to sue him in the Civil Court of the Second Special District for abandonment and adultery, requesting a divorce. Under repeated questioning, Zhang admitted to having an affair with a woman named Xiao Ayuan, but claimed that he had broken up with her in September of the previous year and had not abandoned his wife. Zhang's father, Zhang Yunqing, also appeared in court to testify that his son had separated from his mistress. The case had originally been declared closed. However, because the presiding judge believed that there were still key points in the case that needed to be investigated, he specially revoked the closure of the debate and reopened the debate. On the previous day, the judge, Wu Xiaoke, interrogated both parties and their witnesses in Civil Court No. 7. The defendant, Zhang Guifu, was represented by lawyer Xue Jiaqi, who argued that the defendant's admission during the previous hearing that he had broken up with his mistress in September of the previous year was a mistake. In fact, the defendant had an affair with Xiao Ayuan, also known as Hu Lao'er, or Wu Caiyun, in the spring of 1931. Later, with the plaintiff's consent, he took her as a concubine. In October of that year, due to a disagreement between the wife and concubine, the defendant's brother, Guiliang, intervened to mediate. Moreover, in mid-June of the following year, the plaintiff asked lawyer Gu to send a letter to the defendant questioning him. Lawyer Gu's letter can prove that the plaintiff had long known that the defendant had a concubine. Therefore, the plaintiff's lawsuit was beyond the time limit stipulated in Article 1053 of the Civil Code, and the request for divorce was not valid. The plaintiff, Shen Baigui, stated that the letter was not written by the woman who entrusted lawyer Gu. She only found out about her husband's affair in October of the previous year. She and her aunt repeatedly approached her husband to discuss the matter, but he always ignored them. Her aunt, Zhang Shen, is present in court to testify to this. Judge Guan summoned Zhang Shen to the court, and she testified that her son, Zhang Guifu, had an affair in October of the previous year. The woman and the daughter-in-law repeatedly blamed him, but he ignored them. This is the truth. The defendant's lawyer then stated that the witness, Zhang Shen, was actually the plaintiff's mother. Zhang Shen had a relationship with the defendant's father and

Allowed the plaintiff, Shen Baigui, to marry the defendant. Such a witness cannot testify in court and should be clearly investigated. Judge Wu examined the testimony and ordered the hearing to be adjourned for further examination.

Conversation Meeting of the Nan City Branch of the Rickshaw Industry Association 162

The Shanghai Rickshaw Industry Association, in order to help rickshaw pullers and prevent theft and extortion, held a conversation meeting for members of the Nan City branch yesterday (the 1st) at 10:00 AM at the association's Shi Cai Department. 130 members attended the meeting. The presidium, Qiu Chunshan, Zhang Huaiyang, and Song Yaokun, followed the formalities. Chairman Qiu Chunshan reported on the purpose of the meeting, and Zhang Huaiyang and Song Yaokun reported on the association's situation. Then, the following were discussed: (1) The resolution on preventing theft and extortion was that the association would hire three investigators. If a rickshaw is stolen, the investigators will be responsible for investigating. If they cannot find it, the association will subsidize one-third of the loss, the rickshaw owner will bear one-third, and the rickshaw puller will bear one-third. The Municipal Public Security Bureau will also be asked to assist in the handling of the case. (2) Negotiations on the issue of the French Concession stripping off licenses. (3) Relief for rickshaw operators who cannot obtain licenses. The above two cases were discussed together. It was resolved that (1) the association would request assistance from the Chinese Taxpayers' Association in the French Concession to conduct negotiations; (2) those who have already paid for French Concession licenses should be registered immediately; (3) Zhao Jinyuan, Li Bingyi, and Yu Dajin were elected to review the cases of rickshaw operators who cannot obtain licenses in order to prevent fraud; (4) The Municipal Government should reorganize rickshaws in the city, and the association should express its views on this. It was resolved that (1) all rickshaw operators in the city should be notified to automatically rectify and pay attention to the cleanliness of their rickshaws, and to improve the treatment of rickshaw pullers; (2) the association will collect opinions on the reorganization of rickshaws from all members within one week, then compile them into a systematic opinion and report it to the Municipal Government for adoption; (5) A special donation of 2 jiao of silver will be collected from each rickshaw in Nan City in April for charitable causes (such as providing medical care and tea) and for office expenses for handling theft cases. The meeting adjourned after these discussions.

Let's "Respectfully Return" It! 171

Recently, we have received many letters, all wanting to read ancient poetry and classical books. One reader even borrowed a book about Tao Yuanming's life, but returned it to the library before finishing it. He said, "In the midst of a busy day, where can I find the time to read our books?" But in our opinion, this may not be the case. His inability to read is not due to being busy or lacking time, but perhaps because the books he is reading do not interest him and lack the power to attract him. That's why he quickly returned it. For example, the book he borrowed, "Tao Yuanming's Life," should indeed be "respectfully returned" and not read. Because reading these books not only fails to inspire ambition but also fails to point out a path of upward progress and struggle. Instead, it carries the danger of leading people to decadence, evading reality, and pursuing a world of fantasy. Therefore, we will use this incident as a starting point to discuss whether reading classical books benefits the general public.

There are many books with the above-mentioned problems. They can be roughly divided into two types: one type is where the things described in the book have already passed, and the words spoken can no longer be applied to the present. For example, in the book "Mencius," Mencius advocated for ancient reforms, describing the social systems of ancient sage kings and wise men, such as the eras of Wen, Wu, and Yi Yin, in a persuasive manner, setting out a set of rules for governing the country and bringing peace to the world, hoping that later generations would imitate them. However, we know that the relationship between the state and the people is no longer based on the principle of monarchs governing the people. What use are those methods of "governing the people"? Although we generally have to pay taxes now, we do not have to work for the emperor's family. Therefore, the proposal to reduce corvée labor for emperors and princes is fundamentally out of step with the times. Another type of book is one where, due to dissatisfaction with life and the lack of ways to improve it, people evade reality and specialize in pursuing an ideal paradise, but the result is decadence and passivity. Most of the classical books, from the Four Books and Five Classics to the collections of various scholars, can be said to belong to the former type. The latter includes the poems of many ancient poets, such as Ruan Ji and Tao Yuanming, all the way to the recent martial arts novels.

We can suffer both of the above-mentioned disadvantages when reading Tao Yuanming's works and everything related to him. Therefore, we take him as an example to explain the reasons why we oppose the general public reading ancient poems, classical prose, ancient works, and decadent works.

Tao Yuanming is a unconstrained poet. Most people think that his poems are not decadent but are unrestrained and free from vulgarity. However, we believe that he evades reality, and evading reality is a sign of frustrated ambition and a shortcut to decadence.

A person is not born to evade reality. The reason for doing so is entirely because the cruel whip of the real world has shattered his beautiful dreams, making it impossible for him to obtain them in the real world. Therefore, he regards all practical life as "vulgar" and "sordid" and pursues it spiritually, fantasizing about a mysterious and wonderful paradise. Tao Yuanming was originally not a decadent person, not a person who put everything in the world out of his mind. This can be seen from his poem "Reproaching My Sons." He had five sons, but they "never liked paper and brush." He disliked Ashu for being lazy, and Ayi for "not loving literature." Ayong and Aduan, even at the age of thirteen, did not recognize "six" and "seven." Atong only knew how to eat pears and chestnuts all day long. He was not happy with any of these sons, but he had no way to change them. So he had to say, "If fate is such, then let's advance the cup." In other words, he said that he should just enjoy himself and not care about anything, because there was no way to manage it. But this only meant ignoring worldly affairs. He had an even more advanced proposition: "Unaware of my own existence, how can I know the value of things?" Forgetting oneself naturally eliminates the need to compete with the world.

But what kind of ideal life did Tao Yuanming pursue? What he pursued was a life where "willows and elms shade the back eaves, peach and plum trees are planted in front of the hall. Vaguely visible are the villages of distant people, and faintly visible are the smoke from the rural settlements. Dogs bark in the deep lanes, and chickens crow in the mulberry gardens. There is no dust or clutter in the courtyard, and the empty room has ample leisure." This idyllic paradise is the farmhouse life of "Changju" and "Jieni" (Changju and Jieni are two people's names, as mentioned in the Analects: "Changju and Jieni plowed together, and Confucius passed by them, and sent Zilu to ask for a ford"). It is a life of finding joy in the Way and not worrying about poverty. However, this kind of life can only be admired, and there is no possibility of achieving it in reality. So the old gentleman had to worry about poverty and had to suffer hardships. He had to say, "Gazing afar, it is difficult to reach, so I turn to thinking about diligent labor." He had to say, "How can farm families not suffer? I cannot refuse this hardship" and "I only wish it to be like this forever, and I do not lament personally tilling the land."

Therefore, if we hold the purpose of reading for practical use and with the intention of solving problems, then when reading Tao Yuanming's works and works about him, we must first answer the following questions:

(1) Should we avoid the pain of life and look for a spiritual paradise elsewhere?

(2) Can we escape the pain of life?

(3) Can we still learn from Tao Yuanming and live his kind of simple, austere farm life?

To be honest, the above questions can only be answered in the negative: because the pain of life cannot be avoided, but must be eradicated at its roots through our efforts. Moreover, like the growth of history and people, when we are old, we look back on the joys of childhood, but we can no longer become children. So we "gaze" at the good life of the ancients, but in reality it is "difficult to reach." We "turn to thinking about diligent labor" and create our own new life. In short, times are evolving, and life in the future will only be better than before. Life under capitalist hegemony is certainly painful, but compared to the feudal era, it is heaven. So we don't need to yearn for the ancient life at all.

Therefore, we should read books that describe the pain of our real life and show us how to relieve this pain, and we should not read those books that are irrelevant to us, because we are people with limited time for reading and who are experiencing great pain in life.

Perhaps some people may doubt that reading the books of the ancients does not necessarily mean imitating the ancients, and even less does it mean being anesthetized by books. Then we can answer this way: our reading is not to become scholars, nor are we people with well-thought-out plans and a foundation of learning. They are waiting for the appropriate spiritual nourishment to cultivate themselves.

In a nutshell, we oppose readers reading any relics of the past society that are far removed from our times. As for those who specialize in literature and the past social system and history, they are naturally to be considered separately.

Chunqiu

Imperial Incense 172

— Originally Written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, Translated by Qin Shouou

▲ Introducing the Original Author

This book was originally in English, titled Imperial Incense, published in 1933 (last year) by the Dodd, Mead & Company in New York. The original author is Princess Der Ling, who also wrote several books such as "Two Years in the Forbidden City" and "Golden Phoenix."

Der Ling was the daughter of Duke Yu Geng of the Manchu Qing Dynasty. Yu Geng had served as an envoy to countries such as England and France in his early years. Therefore, his children followed him to travel in Western countries from a young age and received a high level of Western education. Almost everyone could master four or five languages. There were a total of five siblings, among whom the first and fourth (both male) died early and were unknown. The remaining three enjoyed great fame.

Der Ling was the third child and served in the Qing Palace for a long time. She was the most trusted female official of the Empress Dowager Cixi, and her treatment was better than others. Of course, most of the reason was because the Empress Dowager knew that she had been abroad, could write Western texts, and could speak Western languages!

Later, she married Mr. T. White, who was the American Vice Consul in Shanghai, and soon returned to the United States together. After returning, she worked as a journalist for a newspaper. Our female writer began her writing career at that time, and successively wrote many texts about the secret history of the Qing court and the personal life of the Empress Dowager Cixi. Among them, the most famous one, which already has a translated version, is "Two Years in the Forbidden City."

Although her works are all written in English because they were influenced by her own environment, she also had a good understanding of the literature of her motherland and could write good poems and lyrics. Unfortunately, I don't have any existing ones here that I can introduce.

She is 56 years old this year and is already a venerable old lady. Unfortunately, four or five years ago, she and Mr. T. White had a disagreement and eventually divorced. Divorce is certainly not a big deal in the New World, but we think it is very pitiful that she encountered such a change after the age of fifty. Especially a yellow race person, drifting alone in a foreign country, how desolate and painful is that? (1)

Spring in Zhabei 173

— Weng Hun

Ah! Spring is gradually, gradually, warming the earth: warming people's hearts! Ah! I, with infinite warmth, slowly strolled to the ruined Zhabei!

Ah! Zhabei is so ruined! Broken walls, broken eaves, tiles, gray mud, a mess everywhere! Although there are a few places that are being rebuilt, it is as rare as the morning stars. Ah! The tragedy of war! The fierceness of the enemy!

Ah! Now it is finally the world of the Spring God! Although Zhabei is so ruined, it also brings some business in the ruin. Among the broken walls, broken eaves, tiles, and gray mud, what is that emerald green? It is the tender shoots of spring grass!

Ah! The broken walls are silent: the broken eaves are silent: the tiles are silent: the gray mud is silent: in the desolate spring light, everything in Zhabei is silent! It is silently waiting for the exuberance of this spring grass!

Ah! Spring grass is exuberant! However, exuberant spring grass, but also do not forget that there were many flesh and blood nourishing you that year!

Ah! Spring in Zhabei!

The Past and Present of Contemporary People's Names 174

— Qing Qu

"The Book of Rites, Qu Li" says: "Men at twenty are capped and given a zi (courtesy name)." The "Book of Etiquette, Shi Guan Li" says: "To cap and give a zi is to respect their name." The "Yi, Qian Gua" says: "Unchanging in the world, without forming a name." Therefore, "Shuowen" says: "Name, comes from self-declaration. From mouth, from evening. Evening is dark. In darkness, one cannot see each other, so one uses the mouth to declare oneself." Today's people have names and zi, and the zi is the hao (style name), without difference. Trying to describe the famous people of the past twenty years, one can also feel the difference between the past and the present.

Liu Yazi, twenty years ago was actually named Qiji. His zi was Anru, also known as Yalu, a native of Wujiang. When he was in Shanghai with me at "Tianduo Bao," he was also signed Qing Si, so perhaps even fewer people know this. Hu Puan, from Wan Jing County, Anhui, was originally named Yunyu, zi Puan. Shao Yuanchong, from Shaoxing, Zhejiang, was originally named Yongshu, zi Yiru. And his wife, Zhang Mojun, was originally named Zhaohan. Lü Bicheng, from Jingde, was originally named Duntian, and now even if one asks the women, almost no one remembers it. As for some other scholars: Zhang Taiyan, originally named Binglin, later inherited the learning of the Gu family of Kunshan, changed his name to Jiang, and then used the zi Yanwu of Tinglin, and began to change his hao to Taiyan. When he studied the "Mahayana Treatise on the Awakening of Faith," he also signed "So-and-so, a lay follower of the Buddha after 2383 years of the Buddha's death, in the land of Zhen Dan," or simply wrote "So-and-so, a white-clad follower of Zhen Dan." In the third and fourth years of the Republic, when he lost his freedom at Longquan Temple in Beiping, he named himself "Zhang, a man awaiting death." This old man can be said to be very fond of names. Wang Xishen from Liangxi, was originally named Yunzhang, zi Chunong, another hao was Xishen Cancike, and also signed "a member of the peasant family." Others like Xu Zhuodai, originally named Fulin, zi Zhuyan, more than twenty years ago, signed Banmei. Zheng Zhengqiu, originally named Bochang, another hao was Bainan, also known as Lilisuo Zhu." Even if one claims to be an old hand at the Shanghai scene, perhaps one or two would not know this.
