— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 26: Generously Pledging One's Heart and Forgetting the Family to Serve the Country

Miserably Facing the Jade Mirror, Lamenting My Yearning for People

That kind of scratching-the-itch-from-afar consolation is not only useless to oneself, but rather feels annoying, so it's better not to let him know, which would be cleaner. Thinking so, that pent-up resentment wanted to come out, but she swallowed it back down again. But although this pent-up resentment was swallowed down, the tears in those eyes were impossible to endure any longer, hanging like beads on both cheeks in two strings, dragging to the corners of the mouth. Because the mirror was already dim and couldn't see her reflection, she couldn't see those two lines of tears, and she didn't feel it, so she didn't wipe them away, letting the tears drip from her face onto her clothes. She sat alone in the room, worrying like this in front of the mirror, and it was a windy and rainy night, with the door tightly closed, so she thought that no one would know. However, her hurried entry into the city today and hurried return home were too strange. Although she had said the reason, namely that Miss Huang was not at home, her expression was very unnatural and very suspicious. In addition, she had quietly gone into the room after dinner, which was also a bit strange. Ever since Zhao Ziqiang went on the expedition, Jiang had been paying attention to his actions at all times. How could she ignore his attitude today? So, when Guizhi was shedding tears in front of the mirror under the lamp, Jiang had been secretly watching outside the window for a long time. Originally, she didn't want to come in and comfort him on such a dark night, for fear of alarming Zhao's father. Later, when she saw Guizhi holding Zhao Ziqiang's photo hanging on the wall with both hands, silently facing it, and the tears kept dripping onto the photo, his chest heaving up and down as if he was silently sobbing, Jiang was startled, thinking that he wanted to find a short-sighted way out, so she couldn't help but shout from outside: Old girl, what's wrong with you? Aren't you going to sleep yet? (352)

The Road to Success 176

Makeup 177

— Wei Jing

An ordinary face, just needs to smear some soot on the backstage of the theater, and it becomes Zhang Fei, smear a face full of lime powder, and it is considered Cao Cao. When the play is over, put the face up to the basin, use soap on the face for a while, and then wipe it with a face towel, and it returns to its original appearance.

This kind of thing, in the parlance of the acting industry, is called hooking the face, which is actually what ordinary people call makeup.

Speaking of makeup, I remembered another thing. Once, the author was also playing the field, following a few friends to look for flowers and willows. Among a large group of singing warblers and swallows, I took a fancy to a peach-cheeked and apricot-eyed goddess, beautiful beyond description. So, at the height of my excitement, I extinguished the candle and left the hairpin. When I woke up the next morning and took a look, it was terrible. Several pieces of powder on the face had fallen off, and from the place where the powder had faded, I saw the original skin, not only yellow, but also covered with scorched black freckles, and the skin at the corners of the eyes and forehead showed traces of wrinkles. Hmm, such a face, without lying, my wife may be three or four points more beautiful than her. However, after some time, in a certain place, it was a true coincidence, and I met her again unexpectedly, and she was still like a seventeen- or eighteen-year-old girl, and I couldn't find any hateful signs on her face.

So I had to admire the greatness of makeup. Although it still has to show its original appearance in the end, before it is stripped of its makeup, it does have the power to turn defeat into victory, and the function of changing heads and faces.

Horticulture

Spring Pastoral 178

— Xu Qie

Spring Sister uses her fragrant, sweet, and gentle cherry kisses to gently awaken all natural things on the earth from their winter slumber. Seedlings sprout; flowers bud; branches and trunks all stretch; leaves shed their scales and unfold. The spring sunshine is bright, and the spring air is rich and moist. The whole garden is filled with the colors of spring, intoxicating people's emotions. Since we don't have Shi Chong's Golden Valley, let's learn from Tao Yuanming and live a simple life tending to the fields! In the past, Yuling Zhongzi resigned from his high position to water his garden with a well sweep. When Fan Chi asked to learn about gardening, Confucius said, "I am not as good as an old gardener." The great novelist Tolstoy once pointed to the garden outside the window and said to a friend, "This is my cage of joy; inside it possesses all kinds of medicines that can cure all kinds of diseases in people, without needing to rely on doctors and pharmacies." From this perspective, growing flowers and trees is indeed a refined and profound pursuit. Isn't it a good thing for us to engage in pastoral life? In this bright spring season, let's talk about the pastoral life!

(1) Rapeseed, named because it originated in the Hotan region. One says Lei County is in Shaanxi. Botanically, it belongs to the cruciferous family, along with mustard, shepherd's purse, Chinese cabbage, radish, and turnip. It has four yellow petals arranged in a cross shape. Inside the flower are six stamens, four long and two short, and one pistil, with the stigma divided into two branches to absorb pollen. Inside the flower is also a nectary, providing food for bees and butterflies. The petals have a volatile fragrance that is constantly released into the air to attract insects, because it is an "insect-pollinated flower." The leaves are large and dark green, without petioles, and the leaf base tightly wraps around the stem. After flowering, it forms a purple-brown pod. When ripe, it splits open to release seeds, which are the raw material for rapeseed oil. It can be eaten or used as fuel. In summary, the stems and leaves of rapeseed are rich in nitrogen, calcium, iron, and other essential substances, making it a beneficial vegetable for the human body. The oil is not only a substitute for fuel but also an essential source of fat for the human body. A garden of yellow flowers, a few patches of rapeseed, refreshing to the eyes, palatable and filling to the stomach, truly a treasure.

(2) Peas are papilionaceous plants, also known as legumes, and belong to the same family as redbuds, alfalfa, broad beans, etc. Its flowers are very beautiful, with one banner petal, two wing petals, and two keel petals, forming a butterfly-shaped flower. Inside the flower are ten stamens, nine fused and one free, and one pistil with a hairy stigma, so it is also an "insect-pollinated flower." The leaves are pinnately compound, and the stem end has tendrils, so it can spread on other objects. The fruit is called a "pod," and the seeds can be cooked and eaten, with a delicious taste. The pods and stems and leaves can be used to feed cattle and horses. Other types of beans can also be pressed for oil and made into flour. This is a recent invention and a major export commodity. It is a pity that the three northeastern provinces, which are richest in soybean production, have changed color. I wonder how many rights and interests have been lost! The garden is full of butterflies, vividly alive. Planting a few acres of peas provides both food and enjoyment.

(3) Alfalfa, also known as purple clover, is called "grass beans" in Shanghai and belongs to the same papilionaceous family as peas. It is divided into three main types: one called "purple alfalfa," with stems over a foot tall and purple flowers, very similar to peas. Another is called "yellow alfalfa," with stems spreading on the ground, yellow three-petaled flowers, and sickle-shaped pods. The "Records of the Grand Historian: Biographies of Dayuan" contains the phrase "horses love alfalfa." Later, Han envoys brought its seeds to China, and China has had alfalfa ever since. There is also a type called "wild alfalfa," also known as "southern alfalfa," which is what people in Shanghai call "grass beans." It has many local names. People in Ningbo call it "grass seeds," or "golden flower vegetable," "panqi head," and "purple clover" are also its other names. The stems lie on the ground, and the leaves are composed of three leaflets, with the leaflets being obovate and notched at the top. The flowers are small and yellow, shaped like a small butterfly. The pods are spiral-shaped and covered with many fine thorns. It can be planted throughout southern China, hence the name "southern alfalfa." The roots of both alfalfa and peas have many "root nodules," which are rich in nitrogen and are an excellent fertilizer. Therefore, burying their old roots and stems in the soil is enough to nourish other crops.

(4) Turnip, also known as kohlrabi, is a vegetable plant and also belongs to the cruciferous family. The root is round and fleshy, and the leaves are very large. It is extremely rich in nutrients and has a very sweet taste; it is especially delicious when roasted with pork. It blooms with yellow flowers in the spring, very similar to rapeseed. It is worth planting in the garden! Shao Changheng admired his ancestors who grew melons at Qingmen (Shao Ping) and called himself "Old Gardener of Qingmen." As the world changes rapidly, I regret not being able to leave and become the Old Gardener of Qingmen!

Far Eastern Basketball Preliminary Selection After the Destruction of the Chinese Basketball Hall 179

Proposed to Build an Open-Air Court on the Baseball Field

Rebuilding on the Original Site is Impossible

Fire Loss Estimated at Around 10,000 Yuan

The Chinese Basketball Hall, with a history of ten years, was completely destroyed by last night's fire and is no longer usable. Fortunately, the Sports Advancement Association had fire insurance, so there will be no losses. However, with the Far Eastern basketball preliminary selection imminent, a new venue must be found. According to reporter inquiries, the situation is as follows:

Circumstances of the Fire 180

According to Zhang Huiqing, an association employee who lived in the basketball hall, around 11 o'clock that night, he had not yet fallen asleep when he suddenly heard crackling sounds. Greatly alarmed, he got up to check and saw that the corner window facing the road was on fire. He immediately woke up the servants to fetch water and put out the fire, while Zhang ran to the office to call the fire department. The basketball hall was entirely made of wood and painted with oil paint. By the time Zhang returned, it was beyond saving. Within three-quarters of an hour, it was completely destroyed. What a pity!

Loss Statistics 181

In addition to the complete destruction of the basketball hall, the most regrettable thing was the complete destruction of all the sports equipment stored in the equipment room. The loss is estimated to be over 3,000 to 4,000 yuan, including hurdles and hurdle frames. The Advancement Association issued an order yesterday to purchase replacements because the Far Eastern preliminary selection is imminent. Therefore, including the equipment, the loss is estimated to be around 10,000 yuan. The fire insurance of the Advancement Association is with Shenchang Foreign Firm, totaling 14,000 yuan, it is said. According to Zhang, the fire likely started in the equipment room, but the cause of the fire is unknown.

There is also a plan to build an open-air court in the baseball field, which would be more convenient. However, the plan to rebuild on the original site will definitely not be realized.

Youyou Completely Defeats Jinan in Yesterday's Group A Football Match 187

— 3-0 —

▲ No Score for Either Side in the First Half

▲ Youyou Scores Three Goals in a Row in the Afternoon

Yesterday, in the only Group A match of the Western League Football, Youyou and Jinan met at the baseball field. All the spectators had come with tickets refunded from the previous day, so there were over 3,000 people in attendance. Both sides played cleanly and crisply, a rare good phenomenon in Chinese team matches. In the morning, the two sides exchanged attacks and defenses, making it difficult to distinguish between them. In the second half, Youyou worked hard and scored three goals in a row. Jinan's forwards only had Luo Haiguang as their scoring talent, so they could only listen to Youyou's attacks and were unable to reverse the situation.

The situation was dull, and there was no score for either side. Youyou kicked off, and Zhu Shengfa and Xi Qiaosheng, in a blink of an eye, broke into Jinan's penalty area. Sun Tielui shot at the goal, and Xiao Mei jumped up to block the ball and avert the danger. The Jinan team made a second attempt to break in, but Liu Shizan jumped up and headed the ball out. Zhong Yongsen broke through to the baseline and passed to the center, Sun Tielui put all his strength into a low shot, which Xiao Mei safely caught, eliciting cheers from the audience. Jinan's three forwards also occasionally threatened the enemy, but due to unfamiliar coordination, they achieved little effect. Zhong Yongsen took a shot from 15 yards, but it was blocked by the crossbar. When Liu Shizan and Zhong Yongsen fell down at the same time while tackling the ball, the first half also ended.

The spring clouds suddenly cleared, and Jiaqiu scored. At the beginning of the second half, Youyou immediately adopted strong tactics, repeatedly launching blatant invasions against Jinan. Zhu Shengfa passed horizontally, and Zhong Yongsen shot quickly. Mei Meimei's nine-inch golden lotus saved the day. Suddenly, Meimei abandoned the empty goal and made a return trip. Xi A Qiao quickly shot at the empty goal, shocking the audience. Fortunately, the goal was short, and the ball went high, avoiding a major disaster. But soon, Sun Tielui hovered outside the goal, lingering for a long time, with the Jinan guards watching intently. Unexpectedly, Chen Jiaqiu suddenly burst out and kicked the ball, opening the scoring.

Adding the icing on the cake, Qiaosheng scored. Jinan's Gu Shangqin, as the central commander, lost a city, and his anger can be imagined. So he and Haiguang rallied their troops to serve the country. But after six expeditions to Qishan, it was still difficult to achieve their wishes. Zhong Yongsen penetrated the defense, and Qiaosheng swept the goal with a kick, missing by only a foot. However, troubles arose in front of the Jinan goal, creating a chaotic scene. Liu Shizan ran back and forth, saving many dangerous balls. Meimei also provided warmth and care, being very attentive. Xi Qiaosheng took advantage of the unpreparedness of the opposing team and suddenly seized an opportunity to kick the ball at the goal. The ball was high and fast, and Jinan lost another city.

The Three Arrows of Tianshan, Yongsen Draws His Bow. The captain of the long legs, Xiao Luo, his anger overflowing with written words, commanded the three armies to launch a northern expedition. In the midst of ten thousand horses, he drew his bow and aimed at the red heart, but Tang Yongchun safely caught the ball, otherwise it could have broken through Tang Xian's defense. After a while, the ball went out to the northwest corner, hovering between the southeast. Zhu Shengfa hooked it to the front of the goal, Mei Hongbao turned around to grab it, Zhong Yongsen rushed there like a fly, and sent it into the goal, making the score 3 to 0. After that, Jinan repeatedly tried to make a desperate gamble, but due to bad luck, it was difficult to enter the inner sanctum. Therefore, they were defeated.

Yenching University Appeals for a Million-Dollar Foundation 194

(Beiping Correspondence) Since Yenching University moved from Kuijia Factory in Chongwenmen in the city to its current site in Haidian in the 15th year of the Republic of China, its construction has been completed, and its management is strict. Among the public and private universities in Beiping, it has won the reputation of being the best. In addition to the three colleges of Arts, Sciences, and Law, which are divided into more than 20 departments, there are also facilities such as the Qinghe Town Model Rural Experimental Zone, the Woolen Fabric Improvement and Manufacturing Institute, and primary and secondary schools and kindergartens. The annual expenditure, excluding students' personal expenses, is about one million yuan. The school's foundation mostly comes from the United States. The number of donations from Chinese friends is minimal. Since the global economic depression in the past two years has affected the economic situation in the United States, the price of gold has plummeted, and the exchange rate has decreased. As a result, the school's financial situation has also been slightly strained. However, the school authorities, in addition to reducing school administration and the salaries of faculty and staff, still strive to improve the treatment and facilities for students, so that they can study with peace of mind. According to statistics, the school still needs to subsidize more than 800 yuan per year for each student, in addition to the tuition and accommodation fees. The school currently has more than 800 students, and the annual cost of the students themselves is between 600,000 and 700,000 yuan. Since the beginning of this school year, the school has sought to establish the economic foundation of the school and to encourage Chinese people to help themselves. The Board of Directors has passed a resolution to launch a campaign in China to raise a million-dollar foundation. The school's faculty, students, and alumni have also gladly agreed to take responsibility. The faculty has decided to automatically donate salaries to complete the amount of 100,000 yuan. The students, in addition to donating at least 25 yuan per half-year, must also raise 100 yuan from outside. The alumni are actively working in major ports such as Beiping, Tianjin, Shanghai, and Nanjing. The Beiping alumni have formed 40 ten-person groups, led by Quan Shaowen, a graduate of the school and consultant of Jin City Bank, to carry out all the work. In Tianjin, Zhou Yabo and others are responsible for promoting the fundraising and soliciting donations from outside. Nanjing is also in progress. In Shanghai, Chen Liting and Fang Fuan are responsible for fundraising. In addition, the Chairman of the School Board, Kong Xiangxi, the Vice-Chairman, Yan Huiqing, the President, Zhou Yichun, and the Provost, Situ Leideng, in view of the future development and expansion of the school, which depends on the guidance and assistance of people from all walks of life, have recently jointly invited important figures from the political, academic, and business circles, including Lin Sen, Wang Zhaoming, Song Ziwen, Hu Yuanzhi, Jiang Menglin, Zhang Boling, Wang Xiaolong, and prominent figures from the press, including Shi Liangcai, Wang Boqi, and Dong XianGuang, to be the school's patrons. According to the praise expressed by all parties and the efforts of the school's teachers, students, and alumni, the fundraising of this million-dollar foundation can be achieved.

The Boxer Indemnity of Various Countries and Educational and Cultural Undertakings (1) 195

The Boxer Indemnity was the indemnity taken from our country by 14 countries, including Germany, France, England, Italy, Russia, Austria, the United States, Japan, the Netherlands, Portugal, Sweden, Norway, Spain, and Belgium, in the Xinchou Treaty (i.e., the 27th year of Guangxu) at the end of the Qing Dynasty. According to the treaty, the total amount of the indemnity was approximately 450 million taels of Haikwan silver (i.e., 450 million taels). This indemnity accrued interest at an annual rate of 4%, and the repayment period was limited to 39 years. The total amount of principal and interest was 988,123,815 taels of Haikwan silver. The repayment period began on January 1, 1902, and ended in 1940. It was stipulated that the principal should be repaid once a year and the interest paid twice a year. The sources of indemnity guarantee were roughly divided into three types: (1) various customs revenues, (2) various Changguan revenues, and (3) various salt revenues, so that our country's customs and salt revenues were all in the hands of others.

In the 34th year of the Qing Guangxu period (i.e., 1909), Russia proposed to reduce a portion of the Boxer Indemnity, that is, to return it to China, which would be used to establish Tsinghua School and send students to study in the United States. By the sixth year of the Republic of China, our country declared war on Germany, and thanks to the consent of the Allied countries, there was a proposal to defer the Boxer Indemnity. The Boxer Indemnities of Germany and Austria naturally disappeared due to the declaration of war.

After the 13th year of the Republic of China, Soviet Russia voluntarily abandoned the indemnity, and the United States, France, Belgium, England, Italy, and the Netherlands also successively expressed their willingness to return the indemnity due to China. Unfortunately, due to the unrest in China's situation or other reasons, it was delayed until recent years. Only the United States, France, Belgium, England, and the Netherlands have successively returned the indemnity and formally established an agreement. Its use is determined to be for promoting Chinese education and cultural undertakings, or temporarily transferred to railway transportation, water conservancy, industry, or bank rehabilitation, which is more in line with the political program personally drafted by the Premier in the past to allocate the indemnity entirely for educational funding. As for the Boxer Indemnities of Russia, Japan, Italy, Portugal, Spain, Sweden, and Norway, whether they are said to be returned or not, it is suspected that there is too little benefit to China's educational and cultural undertakings. As for the management plans and distribution of this returned indemnity, they are respectively undertaken by the Board of Directors or the Committee. The following is a brief comparison table of the Boxer Indemnities of the existing management agencies, based on the number and distribution of the Boxer Indemnities returned by various countries compiled by the Ministry of Finance:

Country Current Annual Repayment of Principal and Interest Agreed Distribution

US US$1,919,967.10 US (1) Tsinghua University and expenses for students studying in the United States, (2) cultural education, first to rescue the Sino-French Industrial Bank, and to handle Sino-French education, youth and charitable undertakings

France US$4,028,795.74

Belgium US$621,432.96 After repaying the Hua-Bi Bank's advances, 40% to the Longhai Railway, 35% to the China National Railway, for the purchase of materials from Belgium, and 25% for educational and charitable undertakings.

England £596,481.287 (1) From December of the 11th year of the Republic of China, the British Boxer Indemnity has been deposited in London banks. According to the agreement, in addition to the expenses borne by Article 1, Sections 1 and 3 of the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Regulations in 1925 and the allocation of £265,000 and £200,000 respectively to grant the University of Hong Kong to educate Chinese students and to the Chinese Committee of various universities in London to promote cultural relations between China and England, all will be handed over to the London Purchasing Committee to purchase materials for the construction and development of Chinese National Railways and other materials from England; (2) According to the agreed exchange of notes, half of the British Boxer Indemnity that expires each time will be handed over to the London Purchasing Committee and half to the Chinese Board of Directors to handle Sino-British education and other mutually beneficial specialties, and 65% of the returned indemnity will be used for China's water conservancy undertakings, and 35% will be used for cultural undertakings.

Netherlands 306,605 Florins 289

The status of the Boxer Indemnities returned by various countries is as follows:

▲ The United States' Boxer Indemnity

1. Motivation for Return

The United States took the lead in returning the Boxer Indemnity. At the end of the Qing Dynasty, Liang Cheng, the Chinese Minister to the United States, pointed out that the amount of indemnity paid by China to the United States was excessively high compared to the military expenses and the compensation for the merchants, missionaries, and soldiers of the United States. He specially consulted with the US government to reduce it. In 1909, the US government finally agreed to his request to reduce the amount of the Boxer Indemnity, which would be used to establish Tsinghua School and send students to study in the United States. This so-called reduction is actually the return. The estimated amount is 11 million yuan. This is the beginning of the United States' second implementation of the return of funds to promote Chinese educational undertakings.

Shanghai Branch of the Chinese Educational Film Association Held its Annual Meeting Yesterday 196

▲ The Head Office Dispatched Chu Minyi to Shanghai to Deliver Instructions and Supervise the Election

▲ Lu Shibai, Pan Gongzhan, and Others Elected as Executive and Supervisory Committee Members

▲ Telegram to the National Film Industry to Promote the New Life Movement

▲ Request to the Central Government to Expedite the Establishment of a Film Control Commission

The Shanghai Branch of the Chinese Educational Film Association held its first annual meeting at the Shanghai Municipal Public Education Center at 2:00 PM yesterday to elect executive and supervisory committee members. Details are as follows:

▲ Attendees Members present included Chu Minyi, representative of the Head Office; Jiang Huaisu and Mao Yun, representatives of the Municipal Party Headquarters; Jiang Jianbai, representative of the Municipal Education Bureau; and members Pan Gongzhan (representing Chen Bai), Zheng Zhengqiu, Chen Bai, Yang Minshi, Lu Shibai, Tao Baichuan, Li Zhaohuan, Shao Zuiweng, Li Pingqian, Hu Die, Chen Yumei, Hong Shen, Shen Xiling, Yao Suifeng, Chen Songchun, Chen Dabei, Xu Gongmei, Xu Xinfu, Gao Tianqi, Gao Qianping, Zhang Shichuan, Zhang Liangchun, Cheng Bugao, Cheng Kuanzheng, Tang Jie, Long Jianong, Xiao Ying, Yang Jingyi, Chen Kangran, and over eighty others.

▲ Meeting Proceedings The meeting was chaired by Zheng Zhengqiu. After formal greetings, the chairman gave a report, followed by instructions from Chu Minyi, representing the Head Office, and speeches by Mao Yun, representing the Municipal Party Headquarters, and Jiang Jianbai, representing the Municipal Education Bureau. Jiang Huaisu then delivered a speech, and Chen Bai reported on the association's affairs. Proposals were discussed, the association's charter was amended, and the second executive and supervisory committee members were elected. The meeting adjourned at approximately 5:00 PM.

▲ Chu's Instructions Chu Minyi, representing the Head Office, stated briefly that since attending the establishment of the Shanghai Branch last year, it had been half a year. During this half-year, Shanghai had made extraordinary efforts in popularizing educational films. On behalf of the Head Office, he expressed his gratitude. We know that the power of film is quite great. Any movement, if using film as a tool, is easily effective. Now, Chairman Chiang is promoting the New Life Movement, which is a movement to revive the nation. All localities are implementing it. If we can use film to portray the meaning of the New Life Movement on the silver screen, its propaganda effect will be far greater than any other method. Educational films focus on social education, and the New Life Movement is a movement to improve society. He hoped that after the re-election of the Shanghai Branch, everyone would work together to produce films on the New Life Movement to help realize the New Life Movement, he said.

▲ Proposals Passed (1) Request the Head Office to forward to the Central Government a proposal to expedite the establishment of a National Film Control Commission to facilitate the promotion of the New Life Movement. (2) The association will send letters to the Municipal Party Headquarters, the Municipal Education Bureau, and the Head Office to forward separately to the Central Propaganda Committee, as well as the Ministries of Education, Interior, and Railways, requesting subsidies, and also send letters to the association's honorary members requesting donations to expedite the production of films. (3) The domestic film "Sister Flowers" has been continuously shown in the city for over forty days, breaking the latest record in the Chinese film industry, and its plot and performances have deep value in art and consciousness. The merits of the screenwriter, director, and leading actors should not be buried. It is proposed that the association separately award citations and request the Head Office to forward them to the Central Propaganda Committee for commendation. (4) It is proposed to telegraph all film companies nationwide to unanimously support and promote the New Life Movement advocated by Chairman Chiang. All of the above proposals were passed and handed over to the executive committee for handling.

▲ Election Results The elected executive committee members were Lu Shibai, Chen Heqin, Chen Bai, Yang Minshi, Tong Xingbai, Li Zhaohuan, Zhou Jianyun, and seven others. The alternate executive committee members were Yao Geng, Chen Songchun, Shao Zuiweng, and Xu Gongmei, four people. The supervisory committee members were Pan Gongzhan, Wu Kaixian, Cao Huiqun, Zheng Zhengqiu, and Li Minwei, five people. The alternate supervisory committee members were Bu Wancang, Qiu Qixiang, and Tao Baixun, three people.

▲ Telegram to the National Film Companies Greetings to all film companies nationwide. Since national strength has been insufficient and incidents have been numerous, the people's livelihood has frequently declined, and morality has increasingly fallen into ruin. Foreign troubles are pressing, internal disasters have not ended, and the country is in danger of collapse, like a pile of eggs. The trend of the times is pressing, and the difficult situation is becoming more urgent. This is precisely the time to strive for self-improvement and to plan for survival through transformation. The rise and fall of a country depend on the strength or weakness of its people, and the strength or weakness of the people depends on their way of life. The expression of vitality can be measured by their morality of "acting with constant principles" and their knowledge "used to gather affairs." Now, when we discuss morality in our country, the new has not been established, and the old has been abandoned. When we discuss knowledge, we have no time to impart it, let alone seek creation. Moreover, the mixture is impure, and refinement and crudeness are advancing together, which is a common phenomenon of the transition period. If society becomes accustomed to extravagance and thought becomes decadent, either abandoning themselves or indulging in dissipation, when can the disaster of national destruction be avoided? When can the ridicule of being a "sick man" be cleared? Fortunately, Chairman Chiang, with foresight, resolutely advocated the New Life Movement, so as to awaken those who are lost in illusion and revive the nation. It is truly an urgent task. Therefore, those with knowledge within the country resonated together, and the Party's deliberations were like echoing sounds. The people of this association admired and looked up to him, and secretly rejoiced. If our Chinese nation can innovate and save itself, resolve to cultivate itself, and display its talents and work together upwards, then China will naturally have no worries about sinking into the sea. Furthermore, the importance of the film industry in the New Life Movement should also be emphasized. The mission of film is not only limited to art, but it also bears the responsibility of general social education. Its introduction of knowledge, communication of ideas, promotion of morality, and correction of habits are all closely related to the daily life of the people, and its impact is both deep and significant, which everyone knows. It is unnecessary to cite facts as evidence. For example, in the American Recovery Movement, all films produced by American film companies added the Blue Eagle Movement logo to arouse the people's attention. The intention was very good, and the effect was also great. According to regulations, all kinds of manufactured products must have the New Life Movement logo printed on them from March 1, 1934, which Chairman Chiang has clearly stipulated. Film is also one of the manufactured products, so the film industry should promptly add this logo and add full-text subtitles such as "New Life Knowledge" to arouse the audience's attention and support for this movement at all times. At the same time, in terms of content, any crude, dirty, or unclean actions, as well as extravagant decorations, that are contrary to the principles of the New Life Movement and give the public a bad impression, should be avoided as much as possible unless absolutely necessary. The virtues of propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame should be expressed in clothing, food, housing, and transportation, so that the effect of subtle influence will naturally be greater than any propaganda. The mentality of saving the country and protecting the family should be the same, and all lifelines are tied to breathing. We should breathe out the old and take in the new to seek life. I am ashamed of my humble words, but I am willing to pour out my heart with sincerity. I only hope that you will examine them. The entire membership of the first general meeting of the Shanghai Branch of the Chinese Educational Film Association bows.

Special Report

Three Points on the Contribution of the First Draft of the Constitution to National Education (Part Two) Xie En Gao 206

III. Academic Research Must Stipulate Freedom for the People Academic research has no end, and the state should not restrict it to hinder its progress. Especially in today's China, where academic thought is scarce and research voices are low. Before 1694, various studies in Prussia were completely controlled by religion, so academic thought could not make significant progress. In 1694, a new-style university was founded [Halle University], advocating the principle of "freedom of research," eliminating the shackles of prejudice and external interference. As a result, academic thought suddenly became vigorous. The University of Berlin was established in 1809, and the wind of freedom of research became more intense. Whether it was any faculty of theology, law, medicine, or science, the spirit of criticism was implemented to explore the truth. Before long, theories arose and masters emerged, making Germany the source of academic thought in the world, with eternal glory in history. During the Spring and Autumn and Warring States periods in our country, the monarchs of various countries competed for hegemony, and adopted a laissez-faire policy for speech and thought, so various schools arose and created theories, making unprecedented contributions to scholarship. Historians call it the golden age of Chinese scholarship. After Qin Shihuang unified political power, he settled on one, thought lost its freedom, and scholarship suddenly declined. It can be seen that whether ancient or modern, Chinese or foreign, scholarship flourishes when freedom is granted, and it does not prosper when restrictions are imposed. In recent times, many countries in the world have confirmed the principle of "academic freedom" in their constitutions, such as Poland stipulates that research and publication of results are free, Greece stipulates that art and science are freely taught, and the state is responsible for protecting and developing them, Germany stipulates that art and science and their teaching are free, and the state must protect and reward them, and Estonia stipulates that science, art, and their teaching are free. This draft constitution only stipulates in the chapter on "Rights and Obligations of the People" that "The people have freedom of speech, writing and publication..." and does not confirm in the chapter on "National Education" that "Research and scholarship belong to freedom." In fact, speech, writing and publication are all methods of publishing the results of research. If research cannot be free, even if speech, writing and publication are free, the substance has been severely restricted, which is equal to not being free. If it is to prevent harm to the nation, the state, and society, it is possible to add a proviso "but not to violate the law," and there should definitely not be a prejudice against academic freedom. None of the above three points are included in this draft constitution, but judging from the domestic needs, it seems that they cannot be ignored. I don't know if the gentlemen who are the main drafters and my colleagues in education think so too.

An Elucidation of伤寒 (Typhoid Fever) - 1 207

— Yu Yunxiu

What has been described above are the distinctions ancient people made regarding 伤寒 (typhoid fever), 温热 (warm febrile diseases), and 时行 (epidemic diseases). Generally, these distinctions are based on the Yin-Yang theory and Wang Shuhe's 伤寒例 (Examples of Typhoid Fever). Wu Youke had already made considerable corrections to the inaccuracies, as seen in Wu's 温疫论 (Treatise on Warm Epidemics). Now, I excerpt the essentials below to advocate that there were those who spoke out against the ancients early on. The words of the ancients are not necessarily trustworthy, and this is not a recent realization. Wu Youke said, "The twelve meridians, along with the eight extraordinary meridians, are nothing but the pathways for nourishing qi and blood, circulating throughout the body, and nourishing all its parts. Therefore, the innate primordial qi is present everywhere. When it is not present, numbness and insensitivity occur. The mechanism of creation never ceases to operate. If it does not operate, there will be collapse and death. However, the evils of wind, cold, heat, and dampness cannot coexist with the body's defense mechanisms. Once affected, illness and suffering arise. If not eliminated, there is imminent danger or death. Injury from wind and cold, in mild cases, results in common cold; in severe cases, it results in 伤寒 (typhoid fever). Even in the mildest case of the common cold, there are still symptoms such as headache, body ache, stiffness in the limbs, nasal congestion, hoarse voice, phlegm, cough, and shortness of breath." Chills and fever should immediately indicate illness and cannot be concealed. Now, the severe cold in winter is no small matter. How can it be concealed and only manifest later?" This is Wu's rebuttal of the Yin-Yang theory's statement that "Those who do not become ill immediately have the cold poison stored in their muscles and skin, which transforms into 温病 (warm disease) in spring and into 暑病 (summer disease) in summer." It also refutes the 素問 (Suwen)'s 生氣通天論 (Treatise on the Generation of Qi in Heaven) which states, "Injury from cold in winter inevitably results in 温病 (warm disease) in spring." He directly attacked what had been revered as the medical bible for thousands of years. Wu is truly one of a kind in history. Wu also said, "Furthermore, we must ask what kind of affliction results in immediate illness, and what kind does not. Those who are afflicted and become ill immediately experience headaches as if their heads are splitting, body aches as if they have been beaten, aversion to cold, stiff neck, fever as if burning, sometimes shortness of breath, sometimes vomiting, and in severe cases, convulsions. The six pulses are rapid and frequent, and there is restlessness and unease. Subsequent changes are beyond description. Sudden mismanagement can lead to death. Those who are afflicted but do not become ill immediately feel no sensation at all. Later, it extends to spring and summer. After being afflicted, before it manifests, their diet, daily life, and behavior are normal, and their complexion, voice, and breath are in no way different. The symptoms that eventually manifest are no less severe than those of 伤寒 (typhoid fever). Moreover, injury from wind and cold invariably enters through the skin and surface, and the injury is the same to the defensive qi. The affliction is all due to wind and cold. Why is one oblivious, not aware of being afflicted, and ignorant of being stored, while the other is so sensitive, immediately manifesting, and manifesting violently? Originating from the same source but flowing in different streams, there is a world of difference. Is there no explanation? If there is no explanation, then we know that the origin of 温热 (warm febrile diseases) is not from affliction by wind and cold." Wu believed that the ancients did not provide a clear explanation for the principle of those who are afflicted and become ill immediately versus those who are afflicted and do not become ill immediately. Later generations blindly followed without question and did not think to pursue the origin of this theory, leading to the accumulation of errors and the acceptance of falsehood as truth. Therefore, he questioned it layer by layer. Alas, if our country's medical techniques employed Wu's method of pursuing the basis step by step, one would find absurdity everywhere. Those who can achieve a clear explanation and thus establish themselves in the world are probably one in a thousand. They all echo others and do not understand the reason why. If Wu were alive today, I would not believe that he would not be at the forefront of the medical revolution. Today's old doctors, who adhere to theories without explanation and forcefully act as interpreters, are all sinners against Wu.

Wu also said, "They constantly say that the cold poison is stored between the skin and muscles. The muscles are the body's surface, and the skin is the superficial layer of the skin. In between, every tiny aperture is a place where defensive qi traverses. Even a minor wind and cold causing a common cold cannot be retained and should immediately result in illness. How can it be that severe cold, a killing and fierce qi, affecting the shallowest part of the skin, can be concealed? From this, we can infer that this is impossible." This is Wu's attack on the statement that the cold poison is stored in the muscles and skin.

A Path to National Health: "Health Education" 208

— Weng Zhilong

The health of each individual that constitutes a nation is interlinked with the strength or weakness of that nation. Therefore, in modern European and American countries, health education for the nation is promoted with the greatest effort. It is indeed because, to create future fighters, it is not only in the research and invention of scientific weaponry, but especially in cultivating the general public with resistant physical strength and tenacious spirit. Looking back at our Chinese nation, we are still completely oblivious. The statistics on mortality rates in recent years are truly alarming. The lagging of national health is an obvious fact. Last year, I was ordered to go to Europe to investigate medicine and public health. I felt that the country was competing fiercely for national health, and all were working together for public health as a unified goal. Therefore, health education must be given special attention in our country's current situation. From my humble perspective, it should be carried out in the following three aspects to have any hope of success.

(1) Family Health Education

As the saying goes, early habits become innate, and habits become natural. Therefore, the cultivation of children's habits is extremely important. And the cultivation of habits relies entirely on the family. Parents should first create an environment suitable for hygiene to allow children to live in it. Regarding everything about clothing, food, housing, and all aspects of daily life, both passive defense and active physical education should be constantly explained to them so that they become habits. In addition, attention should also be paid to the imparting of knowledge such as dietary hygiene and sex education. Things like displaying health pictures and explaining the reasons for each health measure should be explained in detail to them without fear of tediousness to consolidate their belief in hygiene. These are all very important. Most of our ordinary families fail to consider this, which is a great pity.

(2) School Health Education

Schools are models of society, and students are members who will participate in various activities in society in the future. Therefore, the cultivation of morality, the cultivation of habits, and the transmission of knowledge and skills are the missions that schools should undertake. If teachers know the importance of health to national health, they should pay special attention to this point and create a scientifically hygienic environment for everything in the school, so that students are influenced by what they see and hear and develop hygienic habits imperceptibly. In addition, detailed explanations should also be given during health class and physical education class to make them understand. It is best to have more posters, models, and slides for them to observe in order to establish their health concepts firmly. When I was in the Ministry of Education discussing the currently established curriculum standards for schools at all levels, I proposed adding health classes to primary and secondary schools, and now it has been confirmed, which is really a fortunate thing. Because students have health knowledge, on the one hand, they can pay attention to personal hygiene and disease prevention; on the other hand, when they return to their families or serve the society in the future, they can also help the family, society, and the country to promote health matters and spread the importance of hygiene, and their power is very great. Most schools at all levels in our country, except for a few that pay attention, lack complete equipment and cannot discuss this, which is very regrettable. In the future, we should find ways to increase health equipment fees to actively carry out this education.

(3) Social Health Education

Society is the place where the various members of the nation reside. If the environment is poor and unhealthy, health will be affected. This is something that the municipal government should pay special attention to. I think that in addition to the cleanliness of streets and alleys, the smoothness of waterways, and the arrangement of public health facilities, it is best to set up a health museum in every place where residents gather, with models, specimens, and posters of clothing, food, housing, and transportation, so that residents can often visit and observe them in order to imitate and improve. We should also hold more health lectures, inviting those with medical and health knowledge to give lectures often, using posters, statistical tables, slides, and other items to improve residents' health knowledge. Within the health agencies of the municipal government, a public health investigation and guidance department should be organized to conduct investigations and guidance on health matters in each resident's family, using both passive and active measures to improve the health of each resident. It is best to have a public hospital in every place, and this kind of organization should be attached to it. From this, the municipal government's public health budget should also be determined in advance, and ample funding should be raised to engage in this.

What has been said above is merely what I have felt and expressed randomly. As for the specific plan for carrying out health education, I will draft it when I have leisure to correct it with domestic experts and seek its realization.

Common Knowledge of Diseases - Q&A 209

— Cheng Hanzhang

(2) (15) Scarlet Fever (Continued)

(Q) Does the tongue of a scarlet fever patient have any special characteristics?

(A) Yes. In the prodromal stage, there is a peculiar grayish-white thick coating, which gradually peels off, and the entire surface becomes scarlet red with swollen papillae. (Called a cat tongue, also known as a raspberry tongue)

(Q) What changes occur in the patient's urine?

(A) The urine contains protein and ketone bodies.

(Q) What changes occur in the spleen?

(A) The spleen of scarlet fever patients has a mild swelling.

(Q) What are the symptoms in the recovery period?

(A) In the recovery period, there is flaky or membranous skin peeling. The areas that were first rashy peel first. That is, the neck peels off first.

(Q) What are the complications of scarlet fever patients?

(A) The most common complications are lesions in the throat, kidneys, heart, and joints.

(Q) What are the throat complications like?

(A) The throat becomes inflamed, ulcerated, with fibrin deposition, forming a yellowish-white coating, very similar to diphtheria.

(Q) What are the kidney complications like?

(A) Proteinuria appears early; nephritis comes in the third week, which is very important; at that time, the body temperature rises again, the face swells, the whole body swells, and symptoms such as ascites and pleural effusion appear. Urine output decreases; most have hemorrhagic urine. There is a large amount of protein in the urine, containing a large number of epithelial cells, cylinders, and blood cells. Uremia often occurs.

(Q) How many days does it take for this scarlet fever nephritis to heal itself?

(A) It takes one or two weeks to get better; it then transitions to secondary contracted kidneys.

(Q) What are the heart complications like?

(A) Heart complications often involve endocarditis, myocarditis, and pericarditis. The pulse is very frequent (sometimes reaching 140-150).

(Q) What are the joint complications like?

(A) The upper and lower limb joints, such as fingers and knees, show swelling, pain, fever, and even suppuration.

(Q) How does one approach the diagnosis of scarlet fever?

(A) Diagnosis is not very difficult by starting with high fever, angina, rash, raspberry tongue, membranous peeling, and swelling of the cervical lymph nodes.

(Q) What is the prognosis of scarlet fever, good or bad?

(A) Mostly unfavorable, with a mortality rate of about 3% to 10%. Cases with necrosis of the throat, kidney inflammation, and heart disease are all dangerous signs.

(Q) How should scarlet fever be treated?

(A) The patient should be ordered to rest quietly and prevent dryness in the room, allowing steam to dissipate within the sickroom. Food should be liquid or semi-liquid. Disinfectant ointment should be applied to the skin. Gargle with hydrogen peroxide or potassium chlorate water, apply an ice pack to the neck, and take diuretics and cardiac tonics internally. Injection of scarlet fever therapeutic serum is effective in the early stages. (End)

Can Kerosene Treat Lung Disease? 210

— Yang Yusheng, from Tokyo, Japan

There is a very bad trend in our country that must be recognized! That is, various undertakings in the country are lagging behind everywhere, but people like to adopt the latest theories from the West, blindly following them without careful examination. Therefore, in the past few decades, all culture has made no progress, which is truly lamentable!

Recently, in the medical field, I read in Shanghai newspapers that someone strongly advocated that kerosene can cure lung disease. As a result, many lung disease patients rashly tried it. I do not know the result, but to prevent harm and to think of patients suffering unnecessary pain, I must sincerely advise against it!

The idea that kerosene can treat disease was announced by Japanese individuals such as Hayami Toraichi and Iwamoto Yoshitora. It is a new therapy advocated in Japan. Lung disease is a very chronic and difficult-to-cure disease. Now that there is such a miraculously effective method, who would not gladly follow it? However, famous experts in Japan who possess the greatest authority in medical knowledge, after conducting detailed experiments, found that drinking kerosene is not only useless but also extremely dangerous.

Page 16

Director of Pharmacology at the Faculty of Medicine of the University of Tokyo, Hayashi Haruo, said: The treatment of lung disease lies entirely in recuperation. The kerosene treatment is completely a popular saying and a misrepresentation, and is extremely unreliable.

Dr. Hirai Fumio, a medical doctor at Keio Hospital in Japan, published a long article (see the Japanese Yomiuri Shimbun, January 28, Showa 9), the conclusion of which stated that through various experiments, tubercle bacilli (結核菌) show greater resistance to lipoid substances than other bacteria. Kerosene is definitely not an effective bactericide. If patients like to drink kerosene, the bacteria will not be killed, and the valuable human life will be poisoned by kerosene, gradually heading towards death.

Dr. Arakawa Matajiro, the Dean of the Faculty of Medicine of the University of Tokyo, criticized the idea that kerosene can cure lung disease as pure superstition. He is worried and trembling for the 1.5 million patients across Japan. At the same time, Dr. Sato Hidesaburo, the Director of the Tuberculosis Department at the Institute of Infectious Diseases, criticized that using kerosene to treat lung disease is no different from telling patients to swallow mercuric chloride solution to cure lung disease, a similar tragedy.

Dr. Otani Akira, the Director of the Kitazato Institute Hospital, conducted experiments and said that this therapy has no basis. One might speculate that kerosene is a kind of stimulation therapy, similar to what common people call fish fever, garlic, sunlight, and hot spring baths, all of which belong to folk remedies passed down by word of mouth. However, in new medicine, the harms outweigh the benefits.

Recently, I personally visited the Tokyo Municipal Sanatorium outside of the city and researched the possibility of using kerosene to treat lung disease. According to the director of the sanatorium, Tazawa Ryozo, long-term trials on 63 tuberculosis patients, starting with small doses and gradually giving appropriate doses, showed no effect. Furthermore, in some patients, a large dose was tried, which suddenly caused diarrhea and weakness. Many patients experienced belching and vomiting from drinking kerosene; many patients experienced worsened coughing and a slight increase in body temperature from drinking kerosene. Mr. Tazawa divided the tuberculosis patients into several groups: one group drank one 合 (0.18 liters) a day, one group drank once every other day, and one group drank once every three days. The results all caused gastrointestinal symptoms, and their drinking sometimes occurred before meals, sometimes after meals, and sometimes with milk. However, most patients stopped due to distress. During the period of kerosene intake, there were recurrences of hemoptysis. Mr. Tazawa published a trial report in the Japanese Medical News, extremely disapproving of the efficacy of kerosene in treating lung disease.

I am currently staying in Tokyo, investigating recent medical education in Japan. Upon receiving newspapers from my homeland, I found widespread theories about kerosene curing lung disease. Admitting that I do not have such experience, I am using the results of my investigation to sincerely announce it, so that my compatriots with lung disease in our country will not make unnecessary attempts again.

Editor's Note: Physician Yang Yusheng specializes in internal medicine and has been running the West Lake Hospital in Hangzhou for many years, enjoying a great reputation in the field. This time, he went to Japan to investigate medical education and took the opportunity to record the problem of kerosene treatment of lung disease, which has been widely rumored in our country recently, for the reference of the people. This article was received from him from the East, and is specially introduced to society.

A Review of the Work of the Chinese Medical Association Over the Past Year 211

— Zhu Hengbi

Since the first general meeting of the Association was held in Shanghai in October of the 21st year, after its merger, fifteen months have passed. The work done during these fifteen months was largely defined by the general meeting. When implemented, broadly speaking, it concerned: 1. Consolidating the foundation of the Association; 2. Temporary resistance to medical administration; 3. Undertaking special research in Chinese medicine; 4. Encouraging the ethics of members; 5. Protecting and increasing the interests of members (four aspects); 6. Improving publishing and compiling medical handbooks (two aspects). Please allow me to briefly describe each item as follows:

(1) Repaying the Purchase Cost of the Association's Premises

The purchase cost of the Association's premises was 50,000 yuan, originally borrowed and paid by the Association. The Executive Committee resolved to raise funds to repay this amount. During and after the general meeting, approximately 43,000 yuan was raised. Among the members, the largest contribution was 2,800 yuan, and the smallest was 2 yuan. The number of donors reached two-thirds of all members, demonstrating that our members have a genuine understanding of the Association. Therefore, they were able to enthusiastically contribute and fully show their sincerity. The value of the enthusiasm and love for the Association demonstrated by those who donated two yuan is no different from those who donated two thousand eight hundred yuan. Those members who did not contribute before may have been too busy with public affairs, or the notice was not thorough, or they were unaware of the Association's fundraising efforts. It is certainly not a disregard for this effort. This kind of spirit is rarely seen in other academic organizations in our country. It is thought that, as of the date of writing, only a little over 7,000 yuan is still owed. If the members can continue to exert their remaining energy, each donating five yuan, it will be enough to repay the debt and have some left over. It is hoped that this amount can be raised before the next general meeting.

(2) Resistance to the Central Government's Formulation of Regulations for the National Medical Institute

The central government specially established the Ministry of Health to manage the national medical industry, with the intention of being supremely good. However, the National Medical Institute, a redundant organization, was also established. Its initial purpose was to organize traditional Chinese medicine. Recently, it has become increasingly intensified, and it has even demanded that the Executive Yuan divide the so-called "national medicine" and "national drugs" to be managed by the National Medical Institute, while the so-called "Western medicine" and "Western drugs" would still be managed by the Ministry of Health. The entire medical field would be arbitrarily divided into two. The so-called "national medicine" has absolutely no scientific basis, and its detrimental impact on the future of Chinese medicine is self-evident. Recognizing this, the Association specifically dispatched Doctors Niu Huisheng and Yan Fuqing to meet with Presidents Wang and Sun of the Executive and Legislative Yuans to strongly argue against it. They also presented petitions to the Legislative Yuan and sent letters to each legislator, stating the reasons why the regulations for the National Medical Institute should not be established. As a result, although there were many enlightened members of the Legislative Yuan who denounced its absurdity, there were still a few with preconceived notions who insisted on passing it. Although it was slightly different from the original proposal, it still inevitably regressed. This Association considers this to be a huge stain on our country's health administration.

(3) Promoting Medical Research Work

There are numerous medical problems in our country that need to be researched. If they are like scattered fragments, lacking a systematic approach, with each working independently and without connection, it will inevitably lead to a loss of both time and money. The Association specifically organized a Medical Research Committee to design research projects, and appointed Dr. H.G. Earle to oversee it. The research topic for this year is the statistics of epidemics. However, this work cannot be completed in one or two years. Therefore, the Association is raising additional funds to ensure that continuous investigation and research can be carried out, in order to increase the value of the work.

(4) Promoting and Encouraging Medical Ethics

New medicine in our country has only existed for about seventy or eighty years, a very short history. The practitioners in various places are of uneven quality, which has a significant impact on medical ethics. Seeing this trend, in order to protect the lives of the people and improve medical ethics, the Association's Reporting Committee carefully discussed and compiled a booklet of "Physician's Commandments," bound separately in Chinese and English, and sent it to each member as a guide. It also stipulates that if a member violates these commandments, the Association will give advice. If the advice is not followed, a warning will be issued. If the warning is ineffective, the member will be expelled from the Association in order to maintain the purity of all members. It is hoped that all members will deeply sympathize with this, accept the commandments, and put them into practice, so that the medical profession can forever maintain its sacred status.

(5) Editing Magazines

The articles published in the English section of the Association's magazine over the years have all been extremely valuable. Through Mr. Lin Zongyang's management for several years, the content has become increasingly refined. Since the merger of the two associations, the English magazine has been published independently. Not only must each member of the Association have a copy to read from time to time, but also all foreign medical magazines must select and excerpt important information for research. In the past year, this section has been the Association's foremost contribution to its members. In January of last year, with the permission of the members of the Peiping branch, if Mr. Lin travels abroad, other members in Peiping can take over the editorship. This is also very gratifying to all members.

The Association's Chinese magazine is also an important matter for members to publish their experiences and compile new medical knowledge. Thanks to the efforts of the chief editor, Mr. Li Tao, it has been improved to what it is today. Starting from this year, we are seeking further improvement. In addition to the original editors, the Executive Committee has also invited Mr. Yu Yunxiu, Pang Jingzhou, and Song Guobin to be editors, and approved Mr. Yu as the chief editor. It is stipulated that one issue will be published per month, in order to expand the original quality and quantity and to absorb and publish as much as possible the works of doctors who have studied in Germany, Japan, and France. Perhaps readers have also heard of this.

(6) Organizing and Conducting the Physician Training Institute

The number of graduates from medical schools in the country is no less than six or seven thousand. After graduation, there are often no opportunities for further study, which is a pity. The Association has specially raised considerable funds and jointly established the Physician Training Institute with the National Shanghai Medical College, Tongji University Medical College, Shanghai Women's Medical College, Aurora University Medical College, Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau, National Seaport Quarantine Office, Baolong Hospital, and other medical institutions in Shanghai. It brings together the talents and equipment of various institutions and groups to train various courses for doctors from home and abroad to study at the institute. The courses that have already been opened include pulmonary tuberculosis, internal medicine, orthopedics, public health, pathology, and biochemistry. The study period is at least three weeks and at most four months. The length of the courses depends entirely on the nature of the subject and the doctor's wishes. The total number of students has reached 40. It is hoped that in the future, those who are interested in studying will enthusiastically register for the courses. This is especially what we hope for.

(7) Guaranteeing the Business of Physicians

In recent years, doctors and patients often have disputes due to business relationships, and even become involved in lawsuits. There are often cases where patients fabricate charges against doctors with unfounded methods. In order to protect the legitimate interests of its members, the Association has repeatedly spoken out against injustice. To the best of its ability, it has devoted its full energy to dealing with it. For example, in the recent case of the dispute over cerebrospinal meningitis serum in Hefei, Dr. Zheng Xinjian of Hefei Hospital was accused. The Association impartially sought opinions from domestic experts after learning the truth of the matter. As a result, everyone agreed that Dr. Zheng had no errors in terms of academic theory. Therefore, the Association synthesized the opinions of various experts and submitted them to the court for analysis, and the injustice was revealed. Other similar cases are not unique. The Association has done its best to find ways to protect them, in order to fulfill its legal duty.

(8) Organizing and Expanding the Library

There is no large-scale specialized library of medical books in the country. Especially in Shanghai, there are many Chinese and foreign doctors, but the books available for reference are very incomplete. Even if there are one or two institutions with considerable collections, the types are often biased towards the aspects they particularly focus on. Those who are not experts in a certain field cannot use them, and the effect of popularization is ultimately impossible to achieve. The Association has specifically opened a library within the Association to widely collect and store books. In the shortest possible time, it plans to comprehensively collect all the medical books from schools and institutions in Shanghai and compile a general catalog for the reference of members in various places.

(9) Compiling, Translating, and Selling Medical Books

The Association's Compilation and Translation Department was originally merged from the former Bo Yi Hui Compilation and Translation Department. However, in order to increase publishing, the Association specially raised funds and hired Mr. Huang Yiqing, who has extensive experience in compiling and translating medical books, to join the work. A medical book distribution office was also specially established within the Association to promote sales and facilitate direct ordering by members.

(10) Compiling the Fourth Edition of the Medical Guide

The Medical Guide has been published in three editions. With each edition, the information has been continuously increased. The increase in the collection for the fourth edition is even greater. The original single volume had to be divided into two parts: a Chinese version and an English version. The Chinese version has already been printed. It contains address maps of important cities with sixteen maps, a survey of the conditions of twenty-six medical colleges, an overview of the health agencies under the Ministry of Health and the Health Laboratory Department, a concise survey of hospitals in various provinces with four hundred and twenty-four entries, a directory of the names and addresses of more than four thousand physicians, as well as a record of the medical schools surveyed, various important medical regulations, and a catalog of national medical and pharmaceutical periodicals currently in circulation. The wealth of information collected far exceeds the third edition. The English version has also been started and is expected to be published around June or July.

In other matters, such as members registering with the Ministry of Health and applying for certificates, the Association has handled no less than 200 cases in the past year. The medical community has held more than 100 meetings in the Association. Running around and making arrangements has also been quite busy. However, the staff of the Association believes that the Association is organized by colleagues in the medical community, and of course, it should do its best to serve the medical community. If the members have any requests, they will naturally do their best to serve and not be afraid of hard work.

Experiments on Curing Pulmonary Tuberculosis with Kerosene (Fourth Continuation) 212

— Ding Huikang

(5) I Tried It Because I Was Told by a Patient That Kerosene Can Cure Lung Disease

(I Am Also One of Those Who Tried Taking Kerosene Myself and Believe It Is Effective)

Talk by Dr. Chiba Masayoshi, Internal Medicine, Settsu Hospital, Kobe City

Kerosene is harmless to the human body. I knew this when I saw a car driver calmly drink gasoline when I was a student. There was a case of a child accidentally drinking kerosene, and his parents panicked and didn't know what to do. I told them about this and reassured them. But I was told by a patient that kerosene can cure lung disease. To this day, I have examined three patients who have tried drinking kerosene. Among them, there were also those who had fever, diarrhea, and vomiting. But there has not been a worst-case scenario. Most of the results are good.

I myself also used kerosene five watts, drunk three times, because I had abnormalities in the pulmonary hilar lymph nodes. I felt very good and went about my business as usual. I thought I was cured by drinking kerosene.

Regarding the method of drinking kerosene, I think it is better to use inhalation. I also hope to collect X-ray photographs of the therapeutic effect of drinking kerosene and prove it from an academic point of view.

(Postscript by a Friend of the Fang Woman Reporter)

This magazine received a letter from a reader in Kyushu, saying: I heard that kerosene can cure lung disease. Is this true? I was asked to investigate. At first, the reporter thought, how can kerosene cure lung disease? I was afraid to believe it. But because I was entrusted by others, I should naturally conduct a thorough investigation. After starting the investigation, I was surprised by the certainty of its effect.

Regardless of the reason, since there is such a fact, it is naturally impossible to bury it. Moreover, this kerosene therapy is neither a new therapy promoted for profit, nor is it a new drug. It is a therapy that almost does not require spending money.

This therapy can also be said to be the most suitable therapy for the poor. In the past, most therapies, no matter how reasonable and ideal, were often beyond the reach of the poor.

However, what is published here is a kerosene therapy that costs absolutely nothing. Wouldn't it make people jump for joy?

After investigating the experiments of kerosene therapy in curing diseases, there are many examples, almost too many to record.
